O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the medical art with its contents and I have finished it by way of its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with you, which is part of the work by hand, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And for this reason the work by hand is well-treated in our region and is completely different from all others, so it has the science and the knowledge, and there is nothing left to be desired from the force of the hands but the small descriptions in books of the ancient ones that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	For it seems to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of explanation and declaration and abridgment; and will come with the forms of the iron instruments of cauterization, and other tools of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of it, as is appropriate.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of hands found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who engages in this should master the science of anatomy, as Galileo says, to such an extent that he knows the judgment of limbs, and their shapes and connections and separations of bones, and has knowledge of nerves and veins and the number of joints, and movement and resting veins, and the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, it is said by Hippocrates that with hands alone one cannot do anything well, and with work one can; above all in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that he who is not familiar with the things mentioned above should take care not to make a mistake or harm people; so I have often wanted many of those who engage in this science and have abandoned themselves to it without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess out of the scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries in the neck; so much blood flowed that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another foolish man who treated a stone in the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; so he took out a piece of the bladder and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already seen a patient called for an operation, and saw the dislocation of the patient and the size of the stone; and if one operated on him, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another foolish man who took a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the doctors of ignorance drew the break on top of the wound with great pain, leaving no scar in the wound and finished it thus; and he commanded that it should not be removed; and he delayed thus until the leg was completely frozen and the bones came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I did so, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of cure have been tried out or the limb, and it cannot be healed; and the corruption does not cease to spread through the limb as long as the limbs are all lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder that would cause an abscess to become putrid and then inflame because of the evil of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For leprosy, when it is infected with melancholy humor, does not come to touch it except with iron in such a way that all that is corrupted can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, good son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each of these divisions in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For whereas it is necessary that you keep yourself thus, so that the false mirage may not speak ill of you; If you take your weapons in harmony, and undertake your diseases lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be loosed; and leave behind you the expected diseases of grief health; and hold your weapons from that which causes you to doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to another one of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiéens díst en aunes dis amonestemens: "Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez appelez fol mire.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	» I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are on fire and water cauterizations and medical treatments, and the subsequent chapters are ordered from the beginning to the end, as well as the shapes of instruments, the fermness of cauterization, and everything else that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters deal with cutting and piercing, suction cups and wounds, extraction of arrows, and similar things; the chapters are ordered and describe the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters deal with restoring dislocations and torments, and similar things; it is ordered that the heads of the shoulders be cut as little as possible, and that the forms of instruments be described.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work; it is necessary that I speak about the quality of aid and the harm of each color.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and the harm is the most distant word, subtle science and hidden replies; and many wise men would speak about it, and agree with what I say; and I am short of words, for I shorten my speech.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that all kinds of aid cauterize, except for two types of complexions: one hot and moist and the other dry and damp.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together the substance, neither agreed nor said that cautery is great help; and the other said the opposite: that cautery is of no help to disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be cured by hot disease from heat, nor by dryness; and he who says that cautery does great help to hot and dry diseases which come upon men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all ways, there is no more difficulty in this but he who has experienced it, and who knows by long practice the properties of the cautery, and the variety of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the symptoms and the space of time; for the other complexions we have no fear, even though there are cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them agree and are in harmony with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that fire cautery is more effective if it is applied to wounds that have already been treated, and it has much greater beneficial power than cauterization with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is wounded, and does not harm another member at all.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines come from one member to another by moving away, and they bring about the disease of grief through healing; and perhaps for its height and for the power of its substance it does not cause an excess, if there is not an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	I have found this by experience and through the long service and study that I have devoted to this art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore, I apologize for the length of my words, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret which is revealed in fire, and of the quality of the result, how it drives away diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in his explanations; so accept it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be performed at the right time, and they should be prayed over.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate in all times, because the harm that overtakes is prevented by the aid of cauterization; and most importantly, the cauterization is for necessary pains that cannot be delayed until a greater harm comes upon the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think once, my son, as they do; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so as they believe, because cauterization is nothing but medicine that changes the surface, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and is more effective than medicine in terms of its quickness, and for its virtue and nobility.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And if possible, choose a medicine according to the complexion of the sick person and the place where the disease is located and its virtue; and all excesses are united in him by acquiring meat and similar things, unless cauterizes are administered at the place where he has little excess and moisture, as cauterizes of heat due to pain, and similar things, and like pain does not return again; but it happened a little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why the cauterization of the derries is considered a medicine, and that's it; but they don't believe that cauterizing them after medicine is useful, but their intentions are wrong, and this cauterizing of the derries is useful for whatever reason when we administer ways to treat various diseases and they do not work, then let us administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cauterizing the derries is useful for whatever reason when we administer ways to treat various diseases and they do not work, so let us administer the cautery, and it will be useful; but it is not according to the intentions of the foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Li ancien dirent que cauteres d'estrument d'or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualite de l'or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n'est mie voir car je l'ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c'est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d'or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	The ancient ones said that gold-tipped instruments were less prone to rust than those made of iron, and they only mentioned the qualities of gold and its high purity for such instruments; they said that the tips of cauterizing instruments do not cause sores, but this is not true as I have proven it through experience, and I have found that in some people they do. Gold-tipped instruments are more durable than those made of iron, as they claim.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And so we use our fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	For in this chapter on the head of the shoulder, order it so that the view is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	For this cautery with olive oil is for the head, and by reason of moisture and coldness on the head, and because of many humors that descend from the hair, and to the ears, and for many troubles and pain in the teeth and in the jaw, and most importantly for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis and sodomy and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be cleansed with a medicine that softens the head, or three or four times according to the virtue and its effect and its custom for the patient to bear it; and then do the cauterization on the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the cross between your hands, and put your hands on his skin; after that, put the root of your palm on the root of his neck between its two eyes; and let where you came from, if he bleeds, then heat the cautery that is called "olivaire", of which there is this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then place the cross between your hands, and put your hands on his skin; after that, put the root of your palm on the root of his neck between its two eyes; and let where you came from, if he bleeds, then heat the cautery that is called "olivaire", of which there is this shape: And the place on the mark of ink, and make going down and extracting your hand little by little returning; then remove your hand is holly, and reward the place where you see a small bone; and if you do not see it, then start the cautery as long as you see the bone as I told you; after that take a piece of silk, and put wet cotton inside, and put on the mark, and leave it III days; after that put dry cotton on it; and leave it until it is heated up; after that cure the wound with ointment which is called "tetrafarmacon" as long as he is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old man said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it will infect; and for this reason if you apply help quickly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one must leave the fire cautery in place for so long that part of the bone is burned; and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will heal.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another said that one must leave the fire cautery in place so long and press it down so hard that the bone is broken as wide as a woman puts her finger in order for the humors to come out; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one must heal and treat.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of fire cautery do not seem good to me in all cases except those men who have a tendency to fear; and I think that I should leave it longer; for the joint is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we witness with other members; and even more so when the joint of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first impression of the cautery seems good and gentler to me, and from which I act in such a way that it is salutary.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old woman's pain at the top
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the whole head comes to be in chronic pain and lasts for a long time, one must use herbs and pills that are called 'cochie', and head cleansing and oils and poultices; and if one does the cautery that we have just said above, it will not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's head is of strong nature, and that he is not too cold; then cauterize it lightly as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have made the cauterization on each of the head's horns as we have said above, and you make a vessel there; then put the ventuses there; and adjust your hand so that you do not see the bone at all: the patient will feel too much pain from this cauterization than from others, which I will speak about later; and it is necessary for the cornes' cauterizations to be thinner than those with which we cauterize the hair of the head, and this is the shape:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in one part of the head up to the oil, and the headache is prolonged, and the scalp is cleaned with medicines that are different from water, and other cures have not helped: then do cauterization according to two ways, namely fire cauterization and water cauterization.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization of medicine ague is such that you squeeze a bit of aloes, and remove the bark and cover it with oil at the scalp, and then apply it to the head where the pain is in two ways: first, heat it by placing the aloes on fire; second, place it under oil. Then, when it has cooled, rub the oil into the skin; and when it has been rubbed in, leave it there for twelve hours or more; then remove it and apply ointment to the wound, leaving it for two or three days; then cover it with cotton dipped in linseed oil until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of ointment as long as it is healthy; and if you see that this fire cautery is not effective, then take a look at some of the burning medicines that I have written or in the second treatment of medicines that burn.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery if it is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery so that it is this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "clos" because the head is made in the form of a clo or it has I pit of corbeure, and at the middle to a small appearance; and put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, so that half of the pain of the keur is burned; and let go of your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is far away, and runs abundant blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in wax, and put it on the place for III days; then I put cotton wet in butter, and then cure the place of ointment as long as it is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cautery that is called "cultellare", all along the tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	for migraine

de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Which must be cured by fire is only true of those that move with fluidity, as we have said in the division of diseases; and not to apply fire to similar things that come from scorching and spider webs.

de litargie	Of lime.

de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head

de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy

dou poil qui point l’oil	دو شعر که از موهای سر بیرون می‌آید

Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez. Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medicinal fire cautery is that you command the sick person to leave the hairs long and even, then make of parchment the shape of the Myrtle leaf; then take of French soap and hot salt, each one a 1/4 measure, and grind them well together; and do it hastily, so that he does not cool down, then spread on the parchment with the eyes; and if the sickness is only in one eye, then must be applied to both; and pour out cotton moistened in oil into a tin of unguent; and the sick person's eyelids are in your healthy hand and put your thumb on the medicine, and press it little by little every time that the sick person feels the medicine tickle, for he feels the tickle also as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	If you have been sick for a long time, then take this medicine at your tongue.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the blister has passed, if the poultice is raised up, and you see the paper also raised as if it had been raised by fire or by incision; and if so, it is well.

de la cure de fistule par cautere	For the treatment of fistulas by cauterization:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When treating fistulas as we have explained in the section on diseases, and your treatments do not help, then you must apply cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and wipe his eyebrows with a damp cloth or juice of pease on oil; then heat the cautery until it is red hot; and put it on the eyebrow as if it were the shape of a feather, together so that the fire touches both ends; but whatever way you do it, it is best for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula is opened, and treat it with perspiration and dryness; and if it is closed, then operate, and firmly hold the knife; after that place the hot cauldron firmly, and keep your hand away from the cauldron on the part above the oil, so that your hands do not go crazy; and put the cauldron into the fat of the oil, and corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then start the cautery again, and if you need to do it more, let it be for III days; after that put cotton wet in butter on it, and dry out the oinking as long as it is healthy, and if forty days pass and it is still healthy, then put corrosive medicine on it until the bone is uncovered; and heal according to what came to his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I know one way to cauterize a fistula, which no one of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Do you understand a fistula, and seal it up; then put in the slit a subtle thread of which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I make it in the quantity of one.Z. of vinegar; and hold your hand firmly, so that the vinaigrette does not run into its oil; and you put on the oil to the patient wet cotton in a vat or bath: the vinegar thus artfully placed at the site of the fistula, and the sick person is healed per wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the fire that we have spoken about, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then you should administer a punch to the nose, and bring back the fistula to the root of the nose according to what is suitable in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	in the fissures of the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	These times have caused fissures in the lips, which are called "warts", and most often in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fissures as we have said in the divisions, and the cure does not benefit, then in a small cauldron according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it immediately into those fissures as soon as it comes; after the cure, apply the balm of cerote until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the palais or at the roots of the teeth, after having made pus and it has hardened and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit: then it is appropriate that you have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after having closed or pierced the fistula, and keep your hand until the iron comes up to the font of the hole, and do so a time or two; after the cure as we have said, as long as it is healthy; and if it is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to discover the place and remove the corrumpted bone, according to what you will find in his chapter.
dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure this with medicines, then put the head of the sick person in your lap; after that heat the cautery so that its form comes out here in this way that you put a string on the tooth; and put the cautery hot inside, and hold it for so long as your hand feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; then let go of your hand and start again with the cautery according to your will; then fill the mouth of the sick person with salt water, and let it sit there for an hour and wash it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way the tooth which was moving is fixed, and the gums which were softened are tightened, and the moisture which corrupted is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain in the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the teeth comes from cold, or if there is frost or burning, and medicines do not help, then one should use two types of cauterization: fire cauterization and butter cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	A fire cautery: If it is like this, that you squeeze butter from a cow’s udder, and the tip in a spoon of iron or gold; after take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent, and the moisture into butter, and put on the tooth aching gently and keep it as long as it cools down; and so do often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the cotton and the wool are very wet with butter, and put it on the tooth aching, and put a piece of iron hot enough for the fire to come to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	A fire cautery: If it is like this, that you squeeze the juice from a blackberry bush with your fingers, and the tip in a spoon of iron or gold; after take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent, and the juice into a paste, and put on the tooth aching gently and keep it as long as it cools down; and so do often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the cotton is very wet with the juice, and put it on the tooth aching, and put a hot piece of iron onto it, so that the fire comes to the root of the tooth. Put together a fire cautery if it is like this, that you squeeze the juice from a blackberry bush with your fingers, and let the tip be very hot; after take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent, and the juice into a paste, and put on the tooth aching gently and keep it as long as it cools down; make this often, for the pain will increase that same day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the sick person fill his mouth with good butter in the haste of this cautery, and then he takes it away; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a caustic out of the cheek that you want, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the poultice:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of cold moist flumes, and does not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the head of the shoulder according to what you have described above, and make two openings for the fumes to rise on either side of the cautery; and place the cautery hot on the abscess once, wherever it is necessary, until it comes to the root of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it like that for three days; and put cotton soaked in oil and butter on top until the burning is over; then cure the wound with ointment and bandages until it is well.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the leg:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture prevails over the bones and most importantly when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should be voided first by solvents medicines; after that, cauterize at the root of the throat, and keep back from the taste but a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, make another cauterization at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cauterization be what is called a 'clavicle'; and heal the place as we have said before as long as it is healthy.
de la toust	of the toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the diseases of the bones are due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or scorbut, and it is an old disease, then make two cauterizations on the forelock in the furrow; and another cauterization milks between the breasts; and let the cauterizations be what is called a 'clavicle' according to the form which is before you.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, make a cauterization by poking all the way to the "poins" which is called the shape in front of the ear disease; and let the "poins" be up to XXX or less.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment, follow this method described earlier, and let the cauterization be done in three steps according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for those who are less able, do three together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	to prevent the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, place the patient on their back and their side; then apply the fire cautery to the joint in two places as you would with your left hand; and if the joint has dislocated inside, use this form of treatment:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize him until he pierces it up to the coast and comes out with the figure of the cautery together 4 cauteries; and because this is made with the cautery that has 3 nerves, for the figure of the cauterization are 4 cauteries; and they are the nerve according to the subtility of a tent and this is the form of the cautery that has 3 nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is placed on this nerve for there are 8 cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After it is placed on the cautery, grind it with salt; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, such a thing happened, then make the cautery on the thick part of the cautery with a claw, or many cauteries pierce it.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and the moisture is taken from the bone, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come colds and moisture as it is taken out of its composition, and are multiplied to him, and the customs of cures are used, and he does not benefit, then the patient should be carried on his back, and his legs and hands spread out.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From then on he makes three fire cauterions on the shoulder blade from the quantity of a coin, making all the cauterions clavicular, and two cauterions on either side so that they are at three angles as far apart as possible so that they are not joined together when they move, and the cauterion is made so perfect that it burns both sides, and the shape of the cauterions is according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see cauterized with a great cautery the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by piercing and signing on the stomach in one point according to the quantity that you see to encure; then cauterize to all the cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we have had before, until he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	Regarding the liver, when it has pain from cold and moisture and strong wind, until it is freed from its natural composition due to excesses; and the patient is treated for what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him; if he becomes angry at his enemy, sign three cauterizes according to this form, shape, and quantity on the liver, so as to remove the hypocondria, where the cut of the ombel is; and leave a space between each cautery the size of two fingers; and let the cautery of the long neck, and do not press too hard all the way; and let it be burned with moderate heat halfway through; and let the patient lie on his back, and spread his legs, and lift his breasts; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	Et si ta volonté est, que ces cautères de la couture soient scellés, si tu es subtil et sage en l'art, et que tu te gardes de brûler tout le cuir chevelu, car tu pourrais assécher tout le corps; et qu'il n'y ait pas de bouillon, car la couture est très subtile à cet endroit, et c'est par là que l'on voit.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if there is an abscess in the liver, and you need to know whether it is in the fat of the liver or in the membrane: If it is in the fat, then feel that the patient feels little pain; and if it is in the membrane, then feel great pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment of the ulcers has ended, then the patient should be made to lie on his side; and then sign where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which seems like a tooth, so that there is no doubt about it:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I cautery as long as the wounds are burning, and come until syphac, as long as the porreture is all burned; after the cure according to the cure of the sweats as long as he is sane; and it comes to nothing but this cautery use no fire that have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whom these diseases have corrupted not at any time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And then he can take it as hard as possible, and it seems to me that he should leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the plagues,
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	For the pleurisy, the old people said that one should make plagues of root of aristolochia, and in this way: take a root of aristolochia long, the largest that you can find, and dry it, and also make it as long and as thick as your two hands; and soak it in oil, and put it on the fire, and cauterize I cautery between the ligature and the neck, and II small cauteries a little down the part which is desoz the beard; and cauterize II between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining behind a little; and I cautery in the milk, and I another on the stomach, and I between the two shoulders, and II at the cost of the back recently milking the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make it open as if you were smelling it.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no old man uses the fire cautery resembling a razor, and he scatters it and places it between the ribs until he reaches the abscess; and they flee from the pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes out which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the division of treatments, and it does not benefit, then they devoted three ways of cauterizing that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one way is this: you make three cauterizations, or four, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the fire cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and let the patient sweat on his back; and another way of cauterizing is this: you heat the cautery which has two ners, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and apply the cautery to the site of the mouse's cut, or the cuts come from left to right, and let the elevation that you feel by touching according to the length, according to the breadth of the body, and the cauterization be according to the breadth.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After that you put the two nails on fire until the smell is perceived from the other side, and then place the cauldron firmly, and thus in it there will be four. And if you see it, cauterize all of it with three nails.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure has been left to stand for a long time, and this is true that the other cure in front of it must be finished.
de ydropisie	from dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Do not cauterize by the method called "ascultation".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the methods we have described in the divisions, and your cure does not benefit from it, then you must make four cauterizings around the boude (abdominal region), and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the back of the spine, and one on the neck; and let the cauterizings be close to the skin of the cure.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the fire cautery to go away a long time, and do not let the cure of the patient after the cautery; and the healing would hasten, and will be together the two intentions with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the fire cautery for the abdomen is the key that we have before us to explain; and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is described above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the joints
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the joints are swollen in those who are hydrophylic, and are yellow in color, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the index and middle fingers; and raise your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too far in all of it, lest the yellow [color] would be forced out, and the cautery is made according to its form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After, make two cauterizations on each leg at the tip of the knife; and let the cauterization be long, one on the outside of the knee in front and the other behind, facing the foot; and leave the cauterizations for a long time without healing, because they will hurt; after, heal the others as we have said.
de la menoison	of the mansion
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the abdomen comes from cold and moisture, as long as the digestive and nutritious virtue that is in the stomach and in the intestines is affleбл, and cannot be healed by any kind of treatment; and you will see the patient very suffering and of great virtue, so do I make a great cauterization on the stomach according to what it has spoken before or the cauterization of the stomach, circulating; and four cauterizations around the navel carefully a little one, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the knuckle, and a cautery on each finger, and two small cauteries on the stomach, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	in the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at the root, or one or more, and they are old and large humors of cold and moist putrefaction, and are cured as we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit if cauterizations are made: three on the spine of the back, that which is all further away from the anus is poked little by little in triangulating, and one cauterization is applied to the anus two times; and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and you see swelling of the face, then apply a large cauterization to the stomach, as stated above, and another to the liver, and another to the bile at all cauterized places, and leave the cauterization open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After care, let the wound heal until it is well.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh that is called “thel”
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply to the flesh that is called “thel,” if you heat the fire-cauterizer that seems like a razor, and then put it all aflame on the flesh that is coping; and leave it so that the cauterizer comes to the birth of the vein, from which it will not move; do this once or twice, and if there is much of the flesh, cauterize each as we have said; after applying beneficial ointments until they are well; and if you cauterize with a large fire-cauterizer on the armpit, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will tell you in your place, so comes a disease that cannot be cured except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	If there is no outlet for the wind, and it is agitated and vomits pus and moisture, then it must be given an extremely subtle treatment, and you must know exactly how much of the treatment is perfect.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After warming the caustic that seems like a razor, pour it into the fistula according to the quantity by which the treatment entered, and start again with the caustic until the course of the corruption is burned, once or twice, according to the quantity required; and be careful not to harm the nerves that are in there, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula runs along the course of the bladder and intestine, be careful not to harm these veins, and only use fire in a well- heated place, and believe that it is not dangerous; after treating the area until it is healed, and if the matter is dried up, you will know that the area is completely healed; and if the matter is not dried up, you will know that the course has been split, and the bone has rotted at its bottom; and thus as one of these that we will describe in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of the kidneys comes with a strong wind and does not respond to the treatment of women, then it is necessary that you perform a cauterization on the kidneys from both sides with the clavicle cautery that we have mentioned above; and if we perform cauterization in the middle, there will be III cauterizations in line, and greater aid will be done.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from pain and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you perform a cauterization on the back of the bladder, where the hair of the penis comes together, and each cauterization is as long as one inch; and you perform another cauterization behind, where it is necessary to do so; and you perform the clavicle cauterization according to the form described above.
de la marris	of the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the mare is cold and moist, and will not stand for being bred, and the flowers are rotted and come late; and when they come, how much pain they cause: then it is necessary that you make three cauterizations around the udder, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back; and let the cauterizations be clung to, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hindquarter
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends into the socket of the hindquarter, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints are found to be slippery, so it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the socket of the hindquarter with a circular cauterization, and mark in front of the joint around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and if so, let the cauterization be like those with which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have the fire cautery, make three cauterization with olive oil, and let the cauterizations be perfect like all the curers; and treat until he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	for the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When the pain comes in the hip joint, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purging the patient with large pills of fetid pills, or other bad-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After that, make the cauterization; and the manner of the cauterization is according to two manners: that is to say, together with fiery medicines, and fire cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauterization is according to many ways, of which one is: that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauterizations according to this form, and make a good depth and large, and there between each cauterization take the space of two, and let the cauterizations be olive; never do you make a cauterization in the middle on the top of the hip joint, for there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if the cautery of the circle that we have mentioned in front to the dislocation of the hip: but do it in such a way that the circles contain all the hip, and all the flesh of the leg is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes only to the thigh and leg, do two cauterizations on this side where the patient feels the pain, and one on top of the ankle, three or four times; either cut off the skin, or burn the flesh of the leg; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two or three toes or almost to the heel, cauterize that spot three or four times with the "poins" caute
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he is a barber, let him do more; and if it hurts that the pain goes from the groin to the thigh, let him make a fire cautery or circular, and give him good care in all his cauterizations so that you do not leave it longer than necessary so that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and do not cause great harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have made a cauterization on the heel of the foot and left it so long that the leg was completely swollen, and the bones as well, and it became pierced and rotten throughout the bones.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution for the stomach which has brought death.
