de la porriture de l’oil	for the oil rot
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati" or "porridge in oil", comes about in oil, there are two ways to deal with it: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes from a wound, or from the scalpel, or from a cauterizer, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method for opening it is that you cut the seam, and separate the lips of him, and put linen threads inside, and let it heal until it is well; and it does not come that you use in his cure things that dry up and restrain.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will come back worse than before; but use things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and water or ale and flax seed are cooked, and olive oil is melted in any of them, and wrap a tent around him, and cure him from this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you keep yourself guarded so that it does not heal according to its previous form; and what we have said about preventing this disease from returning is that it will not return according to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	from the horse that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is called "ascratic", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident arises from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way to prevent it is that you should take an needle, in which there is a double thread, and pierce it through all the hair of the shoulder, so that the thread comes out at two places on the left side, so that the needle pierces the skin between the two points, and then tighten the thread around the bone, and tie a knot.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is convenient, it is good; if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper over, and make two cuts on either side of the incision that you have made, and let the two pieces be assembled so that their shape is like the shape of a letter X; then remove this paper, according to the quantity that its edges are apart from each other, from the place where the paper was, then join the two parts together, and sew them with another thread; then give the patient the soft medicines that we have mentioned, and bandages, until he is well.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	Et si la maladie vient de fendure ou de couture ou de cautère, il convient que tu fendes une fente large en dehors des poils des papieres, et selon ce qui est ci-devant; puis dévoie entre les deux levres d'une tente, si comme j'ai dit; et il faut faire l'ouvraige selon la forme de la maladie, car elle est très diverse en forme, et les maîtres sages apparilleront engien de tout leur pouvoir comment il faice revenir la figure à sa forme naturelle; et le malade aussi, selon ce qu'il convient d'ouvraire et d'instruments em plusieurs dispositions.

de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil

de la fistule de l’oil	from the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers. de l’issue de l’oil	of the escape of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hairs open up all over the body, and there is no danger of injuring the fingernail, nor any reduction, then you may lay the sick person down; then put leechcups on him where it does not hurt, then put oil on it made of poppy seed and aloe and incense and myrrh, and then strain the oil, and apply it to bands and cloths; and the way the cloths are arranged is that you squeeze the cloths enough to make them wet, and double each one four times, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity of hair they need; then strain the oil from above a hard band, and start again with the leechcups without hurting; then remove the leechcups and leave the oil strained day and night, and let it soften little by little, so you may strain it more; then remove the band after the day and night, and if you see the oil come back, it is good; if not, then start again with the plaster and the band and the leechcups until he is well.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The tearing of woven cloth.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the woven cloth, then opening it up, and coming out like a paper thread so that it is hard to see; therefore, if you cover it over, the openings are such that you pierce an eyelet at the root of the part below until it comes out above, then pierce another eyelet where there is a double thread from the part of the loom; and let the first eyelet be placed according to the disposition; then tighten the double thread and wrap one end of the weave around it, and fasten it well, then pull out the eyelet and place it on another oil moistened with ointment; and leave it until the thread rubs against the weave, then treat the oil with soothing things until the wound is healed; and never restrict the wound with a double woven circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs have gained a good appearance, then pierce them with a thin spetumile that comes perfectly from oil, and draw out the moist albuginous and cut the hairs, and leave it for so long; then remove it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	with oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati," is only oil that is gathered in oil, resembling water coming down, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the work is such that you place the patient on a raised platform and straight, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move it as much as you see the oil come up above your hairs; then set it aside, and do not draw out or break the light, and observe the patient's reaction as if it were water; and if it does not come out, know that it is water, and the coming out of the oil from the hair is as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the sick person sit between your hands, then take the subtile spatumile and strike upon the cornee membrane with it by means of the continued connection with the cornee membrane and the crown, until the bowels come out; and when they are brought forth, let them be distilled into warm acute honeyed oil or acute oil or fenugreek is boiled and honey added, then let other remedies be used until they are healed.
des aigues de l’oil	with the water of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have made the shape of needles in the division, and that which is necessary to pierce; if it is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the sick person sit between your hands away from light because of the sun, and tightly hold the oil, then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the hairs are on the left side, or in your left hand if the hairs are on the right side; then take it in your right hand, if the hairs are on the left side, and place the tip of the instrument at the crown by its thickness on a ray in that shiny membrane of oil at the part of the smaller tear, then pour the "almagda" instrument skillfully, and turn your hand around until it pierces into the shiny membrane of oil, and you will see that "almagda" comes to the hollow thing; and the measure of the path of "almagda" should be completely at the end of the space from the prunelet until the end of the blackness, and this is the crown of the oil; then you will see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the cornee membrane, and then put the instrument again at the level where the aigue is, then express one ray after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he faints now, then see the patient in front of him and the instrument on his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a little while, and then he gets up again, put the force with the instrument, and when it is firmly set in place and does not move, gently remove the alum little by little turning your hand slowly; and then put a bit of pure water there, and let it be from that oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on one side the oily oil where or another moist thing in oil and a lot of water, and bind with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now then, and those who are of our sect, let us put on common broied with a lot of water.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the alum cannot enter the oil because of its hardness, for there are some men who have too hard hairs, then you must squeeze the instrument which is called "alberit", from which this form comes:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so now the conjonction alone, and do not go too far in doing it perfectly, but make it thin, then pour oil, as we have said; and at the end of the work prepare for the patient the sleeping position before, since he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be careful of all movements, and press soft meats, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until three days; then take it off in that same house the most dark, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the time of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you tighten it because the blood rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	As the seventh day comes, you shall remove the ointment before the seventh day, and apply it to him who soothes the abscess; and when it has calmed down, take away the veil and put a patch on his cheek for at least one day, and stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and he will improve; and know that no doctor should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Land of Israel, who told us that in their country it is said that a stone is produced from which water emerges, but I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor have I read about it in any books of the old ones; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that he who does not know them may see them; and they shall be of pure bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And may the head of the two of this very subtleness be, and behind three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the chest on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Now sometimes there are born or born various chards that seem to be scorpions at the base of the feet; and if there is any such one, it has a charcoal-colored head, and if it has a blue-colored head, it is a good thing.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Now in this case of the chards that are souef and not enchancreed, it is good that you should sit the patient between your hands towards the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the fine, subtle water from a spout on these chards, and firmly handle them; for thus shall you be able to sustain them in the bone-shaped structure.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains nothing that cannot be covered, if you open it with the fine, light, subtle instruments so that nothing remains; and if it rises up again or an abscess forms, if the wound heals as it should; and if it is a malignant abscess, then hurry and cauterize it until the wound has healed completely, and easily pour in and out or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the child is in pain, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is healthy; and if the moisture does not break through as it should, know that there is a hard spot in the bone above, which prevents the instrument from cutting: therefore you should put a piece of linen thread a little thick, and hold it tightly with your hands, and leave some space between each knot or less; and let the patient place the thread's end in his nose at his power, and draw it through his nose into his mouth; and many times do this for the child when he goes to school, and it is a light thing for him who does it; then hold the top which comes through the nose with one hand, and the other top which comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel them one after the other while holding us who are holding the thread;
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make this as long as you know that the new wine has corrupted that char, then treat the child, wash the blood, and moisten the child with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose right away as before; make this for three days or more, as long as the ointments corrode all who are delayed from char; and then put a plug of mud into the nose for some days until he is well, and if there is need for dried medicines, use them; and that is the form of the instrument to purify the head, where they distil oils and medicines from the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be of silver or gold, resembling a lamp open, like a plug, and conduct it also; and if you see, make a closed plug, and be the instrument flat to purify the head; and I always have at the head to hold it when they heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the neck from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Several times at the base of the nose is a disease called "telul", which increases and becomes very large, so much so that it can be seen from afar; and for this it is necessary to cut it at the beginning, and to burn the whole bone, then apply the fire cautery or medicine to it; and if you delay in covering it as long as it is big, see if it is hard, of pale color, poor feeling: if not, do not touch it with iron because it is an abscess inflamed, for when you cover it once, much harm comes to the patient; and the abscess is by light touching, not by pale color, and you can see that he can cover it all, then empty the patient and cover him without fear, and cure the place with dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	what the eyes are cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is known that when a solution of continuance comes to one of these cartilage ovulations, it does so little, otherwise in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, whenever one of these cartillagines ovulations occurs, it does so little, otherwise in some men. It is necessary to cut and sew the eyes when the wound is fresh at all its blood; then join the two eyelids with a stitch, then cure until he is healthy; and if the eyelids are torn on one side or the other, you must peel all their skin as long as they heal, then join the two eyelids with a stitch, and tighten them, and powder on powder of dragon's blood, and incense burned; and put on the powders a piece of lead plaster of great or any other plaster at that time, and let it sit until it comes out by itself, then cure it with ointment until he is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to sew it up is this: or with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	A main hands avient within the lips an abscess hard, resembling grains of corn, smaller and greater; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut each one with a knife, and bind it up in pinches and the cop it into each part; then employ the fire the place after the cutting of vitriol, as much as the sun is dried up; and then leave it thus, and cure the place of dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times grow out on the gums a tooth that the old man calls "albulus"; if it is necessary that you support them with tweezers, and cover at their root, and let run the bow or the blood; then put there the fire of vitriol, or other powders restraining and drying up; and if this tooth grows out again after the cutting, and many times, if it is covered a second time, and cauterized: if it does not grow out again after the cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments to cover.
des sordens	of the orders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No order should be placed at the tip of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, ugly and rough scarabs that are; and no time should the tooth be black and yellow and decayed, until the corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is stinky; so it is necessary that you put the sick person between your hands, and his teeth in your mouth, and extract the scarabs or teeth that appear, as long as there is nothing to delay; and thus do of black and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are all gone; and if one is at the first rasion, it is good; if not, begin again on the second day and third, until you have all extracted; and know that teeth need different shapes of instruments to extract, according to what the work demonstrates, because the Razor which we use to extract the scarabs has other shapes than those with which we extract between the teeth; and these shapes should be ready for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure a toothache that you draw it out as soon as possible, for this should not be done at all; for this is a highly infectious substance from which there is no excuse to draw it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	And now when the patient is forced to extract it, you must be certain about the tooth that hurts.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain forces the patient to extract it, and he believes that it is a healthy tooth, and makes him extract the good tooth; and nevertheless the pain does not cease for this, until we have already tried to do this with these gentlemen; and when you are certain about the painful tooth, then it is necessary that you scratch the tooth well with your fingers or small tweezers at first and again, until it is well loosened, then you tighten the tweezers well; and let the patient's jaw be between your knees, and hold it firm so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take one of these tools and push it into each side lightly, and move it around as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the root is poked and wounded, it is necessary that you fill it with cloth where it hurts; and if it is carefully held with pliers, so that it does not break when it is extracted; and it is necessary to cut the gum very well around the tooth to remove it.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you should be careful not to break it and leave a part of it, and let the patient feel more pain from the root than from the first one.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to do so as the ignorant physician does, who, because of his haste and arrogance, breaks the jaw with his hands, and does not administer anything except what we have mentioned; but he brings about great disease by the root because it stays, or because of the jaw that he breaks, just as we often want; and when the root is pulled out, if you wash the hole with wine or water and oil, and remove the skin without pain, so that sometimes when the root is broken, he applies vitriolic acid to it; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, so that the first molars do not move, are long and thick, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be strong limbs so that they do not bend when pulled, and well-made iron, and let them have teeth to hold fast.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains moist when pulled, then you must put cotton and oil on the jaw or make a hole in it.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	while the roots are smooth, then the pliers that are called 'algefri' are put on it, for the head looks like a beak; and let them be made inside like a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you must take off the whole tooth, and put the instrument that is called 'althali', that is a chisel; this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be either small and big so that it does not break, and the root jumps by this, it is good; if not, if you help with all the instruments, from which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps himself with this instrument that has two heads, from which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the rasion of teeth, and this instrument which seems a big pliers, whose is this form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and this instrument is either such that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtilly try themselves by themselves their instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, because there are several diseases where the old teacher does not teach an instrument for the diversity of them; and if it does not break the carriage or other bones, or it might fall, if he seeks the instruments that it is necessary, which I have told you, and helps himself with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be big and firm to hold the bone in place so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return the medicine to its place according to what is appropriate for him, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, then use all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not seem to be in line with the natural shape of the jaw, and their form is ugly, and especially in young women, you must know that the root is below the tooth, and it is not in its right place, and cannot be sewn or filed: then cut; and if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak, and made of iron taken from the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits tight and tight by the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, then take a file with this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aiguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu'il ne se déplace tant qu'il cheiece; puis la plaine en la fin à tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop tranchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l'aspreteit tant qu'il soit igalz, si qu'il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens...
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth loosen...
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the teeth of the blade to some pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not scratch the tongue; then leave it so tight as it can stay, and if it falls or the teeth roll, so force with another wire; if it stays and will serve so all his time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the joining of the II healthy teeth, and the II teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Then if the tooth falls, put it back in its place little by little, as we have said; and do not let anyone who is not skilled or suffer, and never make the shape of a tooth of a bone of a cow, and put it back in its place where it fails, and force it as we have said, and stay and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the tongue of the language
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is lost the tongue comes or nature, that you do not start it first; or by accident of a sore sore; and ovraiges are such that you open the mouth of the sick, and put his head in your own, and let the tongue; then cope the nerve of the large, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is pain or no, and this is sudden from a wound, so you bite the hook and cope of the large, and keep that the cut do not become too perfect, for the artery which is in; and when you have done, lift the water rose and thus, or cold water, then put the tongue on a piece of linen; and soak it each night, that the leach not be able to dry.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood runs, then put vinegar on top; and if it doesn't go away, then cauterize with the slow cauldron, which is good for that; then treat with other treatments until he is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a dark or hard color, so that the patient doesn't feel it, then don't touch it, for it is cancer; and if it declines towards bleached, and there is moisture, then pour oncoïde on it, and make it with a thin spit, and deliver it from one side to the other; and if it runs, then put vinegar on top until it is dried up, then return to your opening as much as you can bear; then lift up the head from that place and from silk, and treat with other treatments until he is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	of the little throat boces which are called "godath", and they are properly called the II amandres, and when you cure them, if as we said in the division, and they are not cured, be careful: If it's an abscess of small size and light color, don't touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it's red and the root is large, don't touch with iron, also for the pain of blood; but let it rest until it's dull, and then take it off, because it would break on its own; and if it's a light-colored abscess, and the root is thin, get ready the instrument to cover it, but first make sure that the abscess is calm and not sore.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then you will place the patient in front of the sun, and his joints should be in good condition, and he opens his mouth and grasps the scalpel between his hands, and presses the tongue to all the instrument, so it is in a silver or golden blade as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Now you press the tongue on all this instrument, and you see the apothecary, if you take the onion and rub it with ambre, and move it strongly above your head; and do not move anything with it, then the cover is put on the instrument, so that there is a form of strength; nevertheless, the heads are curved, and one side towards another, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron of somewhere else:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you take the handle with pliers, so that there is a form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let them be cut on one side and not on the other; and when you have coped one of the ambers, if you do the same with the other in the same way, and afterwards the incision gargarises the patient with hot water, and cold and easily, and the blood goes away without coming, if you gargarise the patient with cooked pomegranate or oak apple juice, or mint leaves, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then treat it so that he is healthy; and never let there be other abscesses in the throat than the two ambers, if they are coped in the same way as the two ambers.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman with an abscess that was lying within her throat, which is to say a small-sized abscess; and had I not very tightly closed up all of the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the conduit that was stopped up, nor eat nor drink, she would have died if she had delayed it for another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had risen two rain-cycles through the two apertures where the drainage was coming from.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	So I hastened then a little, and inserted the hook in one of the two apertures from which the drainage was coming, then lifted it up, and in one go of the hook took out a large portion; then refitted another in the other aperture where the drainage was coming from, and pressed the tongue; after that I inserted the hook into the abscesses, and poured some of it out, and so the conduit in the woman's throat was opened up again, and she began to drink clear water and then wine, and did not cease cutting away at the abscess for a long time; and the abscesses receded again, and filled back up the space that I had cleared out, until they were very large; then I cauterized them inside the throat: so it remained stationary without spreading; and I left those parts, and there was only God who took care of them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the blood runs down from the eye, and it is gone and far away, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, then it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the healing does not benefit, and you see that the cheek abscess is smoothed out, and it is thin, then you should cut it; and if it is round and assembled and is not far away; and it is bloody or of a pink or black color, then you should avoid the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the eye disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, because of its blurring and distance, that you sit the patient in front of the sun, and press its language to the instrument which we have mentioned above; then cut the oncil into the eye, and turn it over, and cut with two instruments as I have said in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you should not cover more than what is superfluous which is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it will grieve the voice and speech; and after incision, use that which we have said in the incision of the two mandrels, and heal until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has doubt about covering; then you must use fire cautery on the painful part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of fire cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head in your hand, and then press the tongue to the instrument that we have said or fire cautery, and confound with sharp water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and employ the movement of this instrument, from which it has this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put a hair on the patient's head where you will apply the medicine, as with a spoon, and place the instrument that we have said or fire cautery on all the medicine on the vein; and let the patient lie on his side so that saliva and spittle run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down the throat, and wound him; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the vein for half an hour, until you see it turn black and the medicine seem to be satisfied; and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton on the back of the neck, so that the cotton dries; then do this often, until the cauterization is complete, and then leave it to dry, and rinse after three or four days. And if you need to reinforce the cauterization of the medicine, if it strengthens, and then after the cauterization cleanse with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the incision, except for cauterization. If it is cured with smoking according to this way, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put them all or any of them in a pot, and pour water easily and make it boil; and the pot is well glued to strong ground, and place the instrument that chives according to this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be of silver or gold, and be the one that is bottle-shaped in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the vein through the tube until the vein is dead; after that begin often, until the vein dries up, and guard that you do not make it at the beginning of the arrival of the abscess hot, for many things happen then; and do not make it except at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, then take a dog's tooth and put it in the mouth of the patient on one side of the cheek, so that the mouth does not become too hot; for the dog's tooth does not cause severe pain, and this remedy is good for all ills.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often times a bone or a fish spine, or nothing at all, comes up; so it is necessary that you should remove what you can see, and press the tongue towards the sun with the entire instrument, so that you can see the object; and if what is stuck does not come out with your efforts, it is necessary to make the patient vomit in such a way that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps, if he vomits, he will swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and you stick a thread into the sponge, and then make him swallow it; and when it reaches its place, if it comes out strongly, then pull hard; and if it does not come out with what we have said, then take an instrument of pitch according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can enter the throat more easily and raise the jaw; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest all of it come out, or push the bone in; and move it so that the patient swallows the instrument, for this is where the trouble comes; if he swallows it, or he pulls it out far enough, equally far.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the fluid from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No medicine will help you if it is not used as I have said in the division, for the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the sick person under the sun, because you press the language to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the fluid, if you draw it out with a small hook or tiny claws that are worth nothing.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a knife, and put it in the throat of the patient, then blow on or cut with the blade, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is coughing up water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and let it swallow, and move it with his hand often; and if soon afterwards he feels the water in his throat, spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit as we have said, then smoke the patient with ashafetida, using the instrument I spoke of in the smoking of the uvula; do this many times, for it will not get stuck in the throat.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the smoking is such that you press it on the place where there are charcoal spots, and let the cover come down over it in the middle, and let the instrument come out through the hole; then pour your smoke onto it, and let the patient put the root of the knife in his mouth, and shut his mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes up to the throat; and the throat will now be moistened, and if it does not spit, then begin the smoking again many times; and make the patient thirsty, and give him salty things and ale, and do not let him drink water; and then the treatment is that he should be taken by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument is like a screwdriver, if there is any blood, as long as one can see it, looks like screwdrivers bent to fit into the throat; and has a resemblance to a stethoscope, and has a roughness of lime, so that whatever it takes, it does not let go; and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the scalpels for the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The mouth of an abscess is, according to what this reminder comes from a book or another in this book, and it varies in piercing and cutting; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its middle resemblance, and from that which he holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the joints where they are twisted.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess at the top is different from that at the base, and the abscess at the twisted part is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if at abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the bowels are dead according to their completeness; and if at such that it is necessary to pierce when they are healed, and do not die according to their completeness, as happens with an abscess in delicate joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come in delicate joints, and one lets them remain pus-filled inside, by chance if the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is in a principal limb, and you delay perforating it as long as it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is in the foundation, then one should pierce it even though it has not been digested completely, so that it does not pus out entirely, and come to form a fistula; and cannot heal in great term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for piercing the abscess which is dead according to completion, and that is when the pain has eased, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the debate and sharpens of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where there is most dependency of the abscess, and where it opens muscles; and let the piercing be long of the neck, and the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and innards and arteries, and all its parts even where there is no plication.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bleed, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in the flesh, if it pricks let the piercing be until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you piercing before that one, if you keep your body stretched out to him, and is plain of mud of dung; and perhaps harden the lips and him deepens from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to which the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you bring small abscesses, small perforations; and in great abscesses, great perforations, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such that are chewed with kur, and covered; when they have been well done as drapelets, and have become soft, so you make them as bubbles: and if there are some that are split in three angles, and if there are some whose cover has been done like a wallet, like an abscess of angers; and if there are some whose cover has been made into a circle, and other cuts and appearance of being covered.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Those who do not have a head, like an abscess on the skin, it is necessary that you pierce it clearly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and has a great boil, and you pierce it, if you do not draw all the boil at once, but draw some part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw no more; do this many times in succession, as the boil comes out completely; but if the patient is of feeble virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men decayed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de veel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is a strong fever that arises from the opening, then administer cold water and do it quickly, and wet the cloth, and place it on the opening many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fever persists, then administer care and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is an arrow, and the base of the aposteme is sore and tender, let you put on tents and drapes wet with wine and oil warm; and if it is gangrenous, and the limb is fleshy, then let you put on drapes wet with water and oil, or with wine and oil cold for three days, as we have said; and then unloose the aposteme and wash it and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is something that can only be understood by all when treating abscesses; but I told you before what to do before treating abscesses, and here is the potion.
des soros	sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or treat small sores, and they are handled by us so that they are in webs, also as the neck of a goose, and there are many resemblances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture as well as birds; and there are some that are hard and rocky at the cutting, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist so that you test all the instrument called "intramuscular", from which the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, and it goes up into the long leg.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, if you do not leave the hair that contains that moisture, for it returns to its place when you leave nothing; then dip in Egyptian ointment, if there is any; otherwise, in water and in oil, and apply the wound, and leave it until the next day; and if it is delayed, treat it with fire.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the cotton has started to come off again on the second day, and the tar, as long as you know that it does not stay with the nail; then treat the wound with ointment at convenient intervals until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess persists without draining, if the wound is shaped like this, then the tar; and pour your vinegar on it, and scorch it on all sides, and put all your cure to work outside the skin where it lies; and if the artery is against you, do what I have told you later.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also make an incision on the abscess if it is painful, and with a scalpel and a curette as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on the abscess that is painful and moist, for it is lighter because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.
