And if there is none of these abscesses or the head that does not have moisture, and I struck those heads of an old woman; and I found the abscess as a heavy, sharp, and blistered stone, and it could not be broken; and if we had hit any of them, we would have made a wound as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, let those that come to the ears and roots of the children be opened completely at their most dependent place, so that the bow can be taken out; and cure them as needed.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times have they come with abscesses to the throat, and have removed the lumps, and have had boils, and never come to another place or sore, and are rotten, and infected one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And every scrofula is properly within its rib, as the nodule and the abscess at the throat, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulae are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malign and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that which you see of good disposition in the throat, and is the color of the flesh, silent on all sides and not deep; so that you must cut it from above, and scorch each part, and the two lips of the mouth together at one time, if you need it, as we have said in the case of abscesses in the throat; and little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor is it too deep so that the hand does not escape, and do not look too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to sew, put vitriolic acid on it, or some powder that clogs blood, and extract the wound; and let it be until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begin to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound has healed, if you return to your work, until you have finished it; then examine your little finger for any small boils, if there are any, cut them and clean them out.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the boil, it only needs that you cut this boil at its root, but tie it with a strong double knot, and let it hang by it without hurting; then bind the wound with wet linen dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then heal.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you catch the whole scrofula, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound and sew them up, so that there is no delay because of its great size.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you listen to cover the root of it, and draw it out firmly, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have a excess, cut them open so that they die; and cut them in the same way as said before, depending on it, then patch them up carefully and with similar things, so that they corrode those who are delayed by corruption; and when the wound is well washed, cure it with ointment,
de squinance	squinance
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	said and spoke about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw one in our land who did it, and it is the scriptural word of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have a squint, it is necessary that the flap of the throat which is called the "epiglottis" be removed; and one should not seek help from him, for all the veins and the blood of the patient are in those who have an abscess warm in the mouth or in the throat or in the two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the vein of the neck, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis so that the strangulation which comes from the obstruction does not occur.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it with III circles or IV a small incision through, between II circles or by the quantity of the incision of the windpipe, not in the cartilage; and if it is convenient to cut the epiglottis so that there is no blockage, and the vessel is long
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece. de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	is called "hernia of the throat", and is a great abscess in color of a yolk, and is very common in women; and it is according to two manners: natural and accidental; or naturally there is no problem.

des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue. And the way to probe an abscess is that you squeeze or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little until you know that the instrument has bitten the flesh, then let it be according to the size of the abscess; then remove the introducer, and take care not to jump.

de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the flesh above it is tight, then many abscesses form and all come to the fledging vein and abscess; and if one knows about the artery, then the abscess should be long and perfect; and when you feel it with your fingers, if you feel a pulling out; and when it is for the vein, then go away from here; and it is foolishness to cover this abscess, and most surely when it is tied up and at the angles and neck and mouth of others and is very great.

When the artery is cut and the flesh above it is tight, then many abscesses form and all come to the fledging vein and abscess; and if one knows about the artery, then the abscess should be long and perfect; and when you feel it with your fingers, if you feel a pulling out; and when it is for the vein, then go away from here; and it is foolishness to cover this abscess, and most surely when it is tied up and at the angles and neck and mouth of others and is very great.

quant li boude ist fuer	When the breast is inflamed
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue. Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, do not restrain it; and if it is due to blood, let it out according to these signs of the large and hard apomes, and set it in place; and if it is due to wind, then it is cold at the chest, and the opening is that you observe its appearance for the wind, or for the blood of the artery, or for the vein.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is appropriate that you leave the healing.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you, or chapister apomes, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it is the intestine or the bile, then order the patient to tie his hair, and lie down flat, then sign all around the bile; then order him to move gently between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with your whole hand, then extend the half of the apome on top of the whole scythe; then fasten it with a strong thread or a piece of strong silk firmly, and let it hang; then operate on the half of the apome extended over the string, and put your index finger there, and feel the intestine; if you find it stuck to the string, then release it, and bottle the intestine at the far end of the abdomen; and if you find the bile, take it to the scythe, and cut off the surplus; and if the artery or vein is against you, go inside, then come back to your work and take two needles, and bottle two threads, and bottle the two needles around what you have made a hole; then stretch the half of the apome over the needles, and if you find it, remove the needles, and leave the place as it is until it rot and die, and cut off the dead tissue by itself; or if you find it thin and rotten, then cure it according to what is appropriate, and cut off the apome as we have said; and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of what is appropriate, and weld the place.
dou chancre	Dou Chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	Dou Chancre: We have spoken in the division of the appearance of chancres, and how it should be treated with medicine, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancres arise from the mother's milk, and from the cuisse [leg], and from similar places, and it must be completely removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, then you must not come close to it, for I have never found one that was cured; nor has anyone ever cured one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in its place and can be removed, as we have said, is to purge the disease of black bile; then make it well before it is manifestly full, then afire the disease with a good fire for the treatment; then pour your boiling water or salt over the disease, and shave it all over, leaving nothing; and let the blood run freely, and press hard on the place in your hand or on any object, and if the blood flow is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize until the wound is stopped; then treat it with other treatments until it is well.
de ydropisie	of droopsie
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	of dropsy
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	and be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	So be cut in two parts. A point, and whatsoever it may be, that he cannot come to the intestine when put in place, and will not blister; then see if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: you must then make a slit on the left side of the navel three times; and if it is for the bile, you must do it on the right side, and if it is for the mucous fluid, you must do it on the left side, so that the sick person lies on the slit that the excesses do not run to the weak leach; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pour it out, and hold your hand on all the spatumil as in cutting when quantity of a thumb or more is put; then pierce the spatumil until the leach comes out, and carry it away, and pour the water into this instrument by which you get this form:

de l’estopement de la verge	of the stop of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born with an imperforate penis, or if it is perforate, it is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary that it should be perforate at all, very subtle skin should be used according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put on the piercing very thin skin of lamb, and bind it and keep it like this for III days or IIII, and when it wants to urinate, if it is closed, let it urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it will not be seen, because the urine that comes out strongly does not leave the close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The hole of the piercing is opened with medicine made from clove oil, as we have said, if it widens.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the piercing in its natural place are scarred, because there is none who has the piercing at the base of the penis, so it cannot urinate unless it raises its penis; and it cannot penetrate by that which the matter cannot come until the testicles, and that is a bad disease.

des pustules de la verge	of the wart
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	There are many times when there is a warty growth in the area of the penis, and it has an ugly appearance; and there are both benign and malignant ones; so that you should squeeze them with a gentle touch, and then clean them thoroughly and put cotton moistened with Egyptian ointment on them; then cure them with ointment until they are well.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the wart is malignant, of a pale color and dripping, you must apply fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it off, and there is some of the wart inside the skin and some outside, you must first remove what is inside; and when it is dried up, take away what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all together, unless the head of the penis is not completely removed, so that there is blackness and corruption in its area and the prepuce; you must cut off everything that is black and rotten, then put on plaster made of honey and flour, which is prepared from the bark of pomegranates and dates, then treat it with other remedies until it is well.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood flows from the injury, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:

And if blood flows from the injury, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form: For the removal of blood, and corruption; And if the foreskin of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary that you tie or lead a piece of string from the tip of the penis, and let the patient urinate; And when the hair has grown at the head of the penis, which has not yet been circumcised, or there is an ulcer or abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape with the scalpel, until the ligaments are loosed, and the foreskin is freed from all sides; And if this is a hard thing to say, then scrape it with the scythe at the tip of the penis and the skin; Then separate them well, and put a thin linen cloth wet in cold water, so that it does not stick again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	is not a difficulty in continuous fashion if like the other wounds; nevertheless when we make this operation of our will, and especially on infants, it is necessary that we do it with great care, and with greater ease for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have it only because we have acquired it by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the most famous and wise men who performed circumcision around the navel, and with force, and altogether a novel thing; so that it is necessary to make it with care, because there are two openings, and by chance if one covers the other, it will delay it.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it happens that it is covered again, and the pain is doubled, and the cleaning which comes from the navel is not assured at the point of the member; and by chance if the nail escapes, it ruins the work, and often happens so that it is not necessary to clean, and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the mouthwashing that is made so well on all the body of man I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, cut it equally on all sides; but let the thread be well twisted around the skin; and may the manner of the first working be so that you make the child think, if he hears, that you do not bind the thread too tightly around the root, and then cause it to rest in all directions as you can; then let it rest between your hands straight, and pull the forces between your hands or your toes that the child does not see them, nor any of the tools; then bottle your hand to the root and blow or cure, and turn it upside down as much as the root of the root is; then wash it well of the filth that is gathered there, then tie the knot of a double thread, then tie it away I from I another thread; and hold it in place with the second thread at the pouce and the little finger, and wrap it between the two threads, then take off the cure gently and turn the root; then let it run poc and poc, because it is the bleeding; and put powder on top of the powder I drapeil glueit of a good cake of eggs cooked in rose water, confit with oil of roses and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and the cure him with other cures until he is well.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for purification if this is: the two shoulders should be soft and smooth, and also the shoulder blades should be long and even.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The mistake of purification if it is when the patient escapes from the incision; therefore, you should stretch it with your thumb, so that the leech makes an abscess; and make it even, and if you can't hold it with your thumb, put it in a vice, and then make it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If he transgresses three days, and the part that is dislocated is swollen, if he leaves it until the abscess has healed, and then removes the skin slightly; if you can move it, and you guard against the part of the penis, it will not hurt him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the sore part of things with powder, which we have said about the treatment of powders, and if the cure goes too far, and it goes up, it will not harm anyone; treat it then, as we have said, as long as it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retentence of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	retentence of urine is due to stone in the kidney, or frozen blood, or bowels, or horse's mane, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not flow, and you see the retentence for the stone that is at the neck or base of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees; and let him place his feet on his back, and extend his belly from above his back, and restrain the patient so that he can lie down as much as he can; and then force the base of the bladder towards the extraction of the stone above, so that the urine flows; and if it does not flow, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must use an instrument called a “syringe”, which has this form: and let it be made of fine light silver, like the feathers of a swallow; and let the tube be a palm long and half, and let it be fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for the discharge of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it to the head of a piece of wool or cotton, and bottle the head into the syringe; and cover the surplus of the wool and bottle it up to the head of the syringe, then oil the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a chair, and raise the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and water; and lightly bottle the syringe into the penis until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis over the bottle; then bottle the syringe up to the bladder, and let the patient go until he reaches the empty thing, and if he does not do so according to this order except that he takes him or she goes there is tor; then untie the thread from all the tied wool, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and make the urine run. And start the syringe again until the bladder is empty, and the patient is comfortable.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When the scorbut or blisters come to the bladder, and it is assembled together, and you see it distilling water and medicine, if done with all the instrument that is called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III perforations: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and let the hair grow by which the medicine flows so that it stops well the vessel without addition, if one can draw the moisture, and pour when the need is; and when you see to move your medicines in the bladder, put the chief of the tube in the moisture, and pour while going; if you pour the moisture into the tube, and then rebound it strongly the going; if it will enter the moisture, and will come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clistere from which one clisters the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	Et est d'argent ou d'archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d'un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenantment, tant que li malaides sente quecelle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n'as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d'oile et de moistor et d'aigue, et le lie en l'estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone and extraction together with medicines; and I said the difference between stone in the head and all the signs, and in which stone one must work the size; and in the bladder and penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder often comes out with children, and this is a sign that it jumps from the bladder like water because of its subtility; and I open it narrowly, and massage the patient's penis, and rub it many times, and then become hard; and it is rooted from its foundations; and the healing of children is light until they are four years old, and great pain in the elderly, and intermediate pain between middle age and old age; and the cure of those who have a great stone is lighter than that of those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, if it is necessary first to purify the patient with a hot bath, in order to draw out all the pus that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For he does not bother at any time to seek the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and turn him upside down and move him so that the stone comes out at the bottom of the bladder, and never put it in place again; then make him sit with his hands between his legs, and his thighs turned upside down so that the bladder hangs downwards; then feel and touch inside; if you feel the stone in space, then hurry to cut on top of the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out when you touch everything, then moisten your little finger of your left hand with oil, if the patient is old, or make your thumb wet, if the patient is young and well-formed; then pour it into its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your thumb, press at the neck of the bladder; then press upwards with your thumb, and pour it out where you can cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to squeeze the bladder in his hand, and he commands that he extends in his right hand the testicles up, and in his left hand he holds the skin which is before the testicles in the part where one makes the waist; then I pour the semen in a cup, for this is how it forms:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between what is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and let it be right on top of the stone, and your two sides should join the fundament, and let the size of the navel be wide from behind, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big; perhaps the press so that the one that is at the fundament does not work; and know that there is part of stone where it has angles and edges: it comes out easily; and if there is a part that is smooth, resembling a globe, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grand; et s'elle ne saute, si convient que tu extrazes sur les tenailles qui sont ainsi comme une lime au chef, pour muer extrquer la pierre si qu'elle n'échappe; ou tu boutte desoz li I instrument subtil corbé au chef; et s'tu ne le peux engigner ensi, si eslarge i poc lout pertus, et s'li sans décort, si l'extraction de vitriole; et s'il y a plus d'une pierre, si bout premier la plus grande au col de la vessie, puis cope sur, puis le trai fur, et les petites après s'il en y a plusors.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If the stone is large, it should be made into a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: he dies, or his urine comes out all at once because his bladder cannot hold it; but nevertheless you push hard to extract it, or to chip it out with chisels, piece by piece; and when you have finished your task, if you employ the wound with ointment of myrrh and aloe and dragon's blood, and bandage it, and put on a wet cloth dipped in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the abscess, then unbind the patient from his collar after three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, if the oil and water are very well separated, then the cure of the wound with astringent and balmy ointments until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come into the wound and corrosions, and congealed blood in the bladder, and is retained by this that it does not jump with urine: then you must put something in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and pour it out; then raise the wound with water and salt and vinegar, and help it in all ways that you can, until it is healed; and it is right that all the urines that you cure him, that you tie his legs, and gather the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is placed in the verge, and lodged there, and the urine cannot come out; then you should cut it many times as I have said above, that you might free it from the size by this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proven this.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron, forge it according to this form, and make it into three angulated pieces of iron rod.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take wire and bend it around the edge of a stone so that it cannot come out from behind; then tap the rod lightly with the hammer until it enters the stone; and turn the rod in your hand little by little, as far as you can drive it into the stone; soon enough there will be urine; then press your hand against what is behind the stone.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this in any way, then take a rod, bend it around the stone, and pull it out with force, taking care not to hurt yourself on the thread, and cleaning up the frozen blood that is in the wound; and treat him until he is well.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is a good thing if the stone remains in women, and if it does not happen, then there is great grief, and it is defended by three things: one is that per chance the woman is virgin; and the second is that we cannot find a woman well knowing who dislodges to the mirth, even if she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that per chance we cannot find a well-knowing woman who dislodges to the mirth, even if she is married. And the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more completely by means of this: for we must make a deeper cut, and there is much fear with it. And if necessity requires it, then you should find a wise woman, and put her on, and if you do not find one, do not search for a married mirth, but rather a virgin; and in the presence of a wise woman in women's life, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her to do that which you command in the examination of the stone; and she should look very well whether she is a virgin: then it is necessary for her to put down her right foot or foundation, and press and urge her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she bleeds, then it is necessary that she move slowly from the entrance of the bladder to the outside, until she reaches the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle where the member is arranged, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her two legs above the stone or outside, and make the incision small first; then pull out the string in the incision as you feel the stone so acutely in the wound until the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and which have rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearance [of the stone], then you will know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not come out, place the vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the stone is well-soaked; then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have aids for yourself in your work by using the tools I told you about in extracting the stone from men; and if it does not come out, it is the artery that has been cut, then sprinkle the powder on the spot and drain blood and pus, and do not repeat this, and leave the stone behind, and do not extract it, for perhaps the patient will die; then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the fire is gone from the wound, and the blood stands, if it returns to your work, as long as the stone is far away.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia in the lower abdomen
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramie aquous is nothing other than gathered moisture or white sapa, which is removed from the seed of the apple, and is called "sapa," and is never properly in the peel of the apple, if one thinks that it is another kind of apple; and this skin between the white sapa, as we have said; and such does not happen.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this Ramie is so weak that it comes from the testicles, and this substance spreads.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And this aquous ramie is of many colors: or it is color declining to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or white, and such happens more often; and these are the signs of distemperation of this gathered thing, for if it is white sapa, as we have said, it is a long head, like an apple, and does not close the testicles, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper towel, then the abscess is reason with a part of the egg white, and because of this it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the leather of the testicles and the white yefac, then it smells bad; so that when you see to know the color of the moisture, then try all the insertive quarter, from which its form is above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, and what comes after the insertive quarter, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we heal it with fire, let the patient be healed according to his power and the repletion of his body; then he sits on his back, on something a little high, and spreads out for him blankets; then he sits on his left side, and commands the minister that he sit on his right, and extends the rod to one of the two ribs between the testicles and the long until the tip, and is your cut all straight while you are cutting the leather of the testicles a little here and there, and the scale smoothly according to the power; then pierce the white yefac with water at a large hole, and drain all the water, and then put on the scales, and raise the yefac upstream; and do not touch the testicles, but only the yefac; cut all or separately the same way the cost of him smoothly, that if you do not cut it well, the water will return; and if the egg was to your work, take it back to its place when you have finished the work of the yefac; then join the two testicles with a stitch, then heal it as you heal the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you lay the eggs that are suspended, in doubt of the decomposition of blood; then copes the coion to all the suspension, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the egg is assembled in two parts together, knowing that these are two branches; then cope the other part as you did with the first one equally, then wash the blood, and put on the wound another wet cloth in oil; and put far from each of the eggs another wet cloth in wine and oil, and put over the two eggs, and cover them with double drapings, and tie them all together according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	And take two drapings, and fill them with woollen cloth according to this form, and are assembled by sewing in the girdle of the breeches, and one of the shoulders prays on the foundation until the back, and the other to the part of the hand; and the other chief on the two arms, and is all assembled the restraining cord in the loop of the breeches; and is not once medicated this ramice of cautery in the form of a thin nail of iron, and is that you prays I cautery with a sharp edge, and pierce those syphons as one time, and scorch them with this sharp cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut it in all ways that you can, as long as you remove everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and keep away from the evaporation of blood, and keep away from the incision on the abscess, and other things, if anything opposes you, or an abscess, or the evaporation of blood, or something else, then treat what opposes you according to what has been said before.

de erratique	de erratique
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If it is close to appearing, if you want to know with your two hands or your right.

des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	are openings of veins that, without surgery, and when these hemorrhoids are old, they become thorny; and we have said in the section on surgery the signs and symptoms, and I will say here those that bring about healing.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thigh, when they are fully grown in the marrow, and do not appear to the touch unless it be by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marrow can be felt, they are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then tie the roots and cut it off at the roots, then powder it with restraining medicines, like blood of dragon and incense, and similar things; then pour water on its heels for an hour, then put it in cold water; and if there is blood, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gal and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and so on, and make a poultice for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if it doesn't stop, put vials on the back and don't hurt; then take another, and the moisture in apple juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, care for the wound until it is well; and what is called 'albachi' is red and resembles a sharp chief, then cover it as I said in The Book of Simple Medicine; and then care for it until it is well.
des apostemes de la marris	The abscesses of the breast
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Various types of abscess can occur in the breast, such as syphilis, piercing abscess, herpes, écoulement, fistules, hemorrhoids, hot abscess, and many other diseases I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I die in this treatise the chaut (hot) which comes to the mare (womb), who is not an aposteme that coils a bow; and if you know the power of iron, then consider that the apostemes are sharp at the beginning of their appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if they turn red, you can see them.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, you should not hurry to pierce it, but let it die as long as the pain is relieved; and then put the patient on a chair, and have two small chairs or steps where she leans her legs apart from the leg; and let her feet be spread, and tie her braids tightly with a good knot; then suctions her breath toward her left coast, and introduce the instrument with which one works the mouth of the womb, after which comes the form; and it is necessary that when you introduce this instrument, you put the ring first in order to know the depth of the womb, so that what enters into the instrument does not come in more perfectly than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the womb with drapes, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it is necessary that he put the spout of the instrument on top, and darken the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et when the abscess is opened and one hands it to the surgeon's knife, if it needs to be covered with meat, let him cover the chief and the stump; and when the bowels are empty, if you put wet tenticles into the wound with oil of roses or green dry oil; place the tenticle on top of the wound all the way down to the root, and place clean wet tenticles on the other side of the root in water or cooked onions; then let him continue the treatment for II days before cleaning with a mixture of water and honey, and then only with water or cooked roots and aristo log; then let him go back to treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has closed over the bone, you must not cook it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the chapter on wounds.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	For the art of childbirth, it is first necessary that she knows the natural shape of childbearing, and the signs are when you see the woman rush down, and yearns to smell the air: then the baby quickly comes out; so you know that these births are according to the natural shape, and the issue is with his head, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to lightly press her belly, so that the baby comes soon; for when he comes out on his head, the second with him, and the married man washes away his superfluities by good purification; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it does not come once upon its feet, and comes from the neck or shoulder, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or often, and is turned around by chance on his collar, and by other evil shapes; so is the art of childbirth that she be wise and subtle in these things, and warn herself of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If a child comes to term naturally, and the mother is in labor, and the virtue of her is weak, so that she sits on a stool or women hold her; and when oil or fenugreek has been cooked, then pour the bath between her two little sputums, whereof this is the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If the second one is split, and the finger is held until the moisture that comes out runs away; and the belly of the woman is pricked until the child drops, and if it does not drop, then the woman should be cleansed with muskellaige of fenugreek with oil of sesame, then she should be pricked and shaken with condiment, and her mouth and nose are covered for an hour: now the child comes.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out first, then they should be gently pried again and again; and if they cannot get in, then the woman should be seated on a bench, and her feet should be raised up; then the bench should be taken off the ground, and the woman should be turned over, so that she does not stand up; and if her hands cannot get in, and the child is dead, then the hands are cut with the knife that has been put there before, and the child is pulled out, and it is even pried.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from delivery of the child between his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes down between his feet, then put him up again little by little until he is straight; and then stretch him little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can he jump just as his knees, then order him to bend, and make it shake with fear; if he jumps, let God be with you.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he does not jump as we have said, then turn him little by little so that he is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then he is light-headed.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not come as we have said, then take muscillaige of alyssum, and oil of sizami, and melted gum, and grind them all together in a mortar; and put it on the nature of the woman inside and away this glue, then let her sit in warm water until she is warm everywhere; and when she has been soaked, then make her sit on a chair, then make her shake and squeeze her mouth and nose, and lightly massage her stomach, because the child is jumping now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child between her legs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if I put my hand on her hands little by little; then she is bound to her neck, and her feet hang down, and she lies on her side; and she brings her hands little by little, and then she presses them against her belly, and pulls out her hair little by little, until she is fully delivered; and the child does not cry, if it takes its feet and moves them, then it moves its belly upwards, then I pour my hands; and I deliver the child little by little; and tell the woman to lean back as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	the delivery of the child who comes with a wide hand hanging down one side at a time
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	If the hand does not come back, then I will make the woman get up and go; if she cannot go, then I will make her lie down on her side, and bring her legs together; then I will apply the muscle relaxant that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then I will make her sit down on a chair, and try to bring back the hand; and deliver the child according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and tell her to lean back as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	The child's delivery from his mother's womb, and he spread his hands wide, and turned his face toward her back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	The delivery of the child from his mother's womb, and he spread his hands wide, and turned his face toward her back. Let the balia take hold of his hand, then slowly and gently turn him over, and when he is right side up, put him on a soft bed; and tell him to stretch out; and when he has done so, let him lie down.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all the second time
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When he comes this way a second time, if the moisture is gone, and if he is put back down on his face and neck, let him not be held back, for the child will die; then put the child back inside her, as long as you have done it right, and tell the woman to stretch out no more: then let her lie down lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born many times, and never three or four at a time; and this is not an unusual thing, and rarely happens.
