And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of great treatment, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the part that I have said, and you have engaged to cure it, and you have seen it clearly, then take a tent of iron or of metal, if the fistula is straight, look at it; and if the fistula is twisted, seek it with a slight tent of plies, for the plies bend around the curvature; and if the fistula has broken hands and you cannot find it well with tents, then cleanse it thoroughly with your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and it is completely cured, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the location where he feels it; and when you truly know the location where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the locations that I have told you, then cure it according to what I have said, and remove the false tissue and the rotten plies that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from the right place, it is necessary that you cure it completely, as much as you can, then put moist tents in medicine water, and pour them on the top of the fistula until the medicine corroded the excess that was reserved at the bottom; and then put oilmens in a melting oil, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cure it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein in your neck gets injured or your principal members get injured, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and bruising, let the king treat it with poultices until it is healed; and if it is not healed, rent it back as before, knowing that you have not yet reached the end: if you uncover and examine until you are at the bottom, then restore the joint; and if it is healed there, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If that does not work, know that the corruption is too profound, so you cannot come there; if there is no other problem than letting nature take its course; and if there is one small corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with pliers, if you extract it with the right tool for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, one by one; and if moisture makes it difficult, and there is no error or fear, then cut and moisture and warm it, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place on the wound something that will cause putrefaction, and let it remain as long as the pus is between the bones, and thereafter the bones will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, so wait for the corruption to become black throughout the bone, then patch up the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption and it has reached the root of the bone, so that it needs to be cut away completely, then mend it with cotton until the bone is healed. And I will tell you of an ulcer that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that entered the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and grew a large abscess, and had no apparent cause for opening; but by their folly they caused it to grow so much that the abscess opened, and corrupted much matter, and became a fistula, and it came to be so bad that all his bones were wet with sweat and moisture from the body; and many times he was cured within two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines they used to cure him, and what ran through the fistula caused great color changes in his body; and his body became red in places, and had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I fixed a tent in one of those holes, and then searched all the holes, and I found that one came out against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and fixed in one of the holes as much as I could discover a part of the bone, and I found it rotten and pierced, and came out corruption to the bone inside; I knew what appeared to me of the bone rotten, and I took care that there was no other corruption, except that which I had; and I began to restore the wound with medicines against long time, and could not be bonded; and then I began again, and discovered the bone so as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I knew it, and then I took it, and leaned over to bond the place; but I could not fix until I fixed within a palm of the bone, and turned it entirely, then I restored it with medicines; and he was healed and bonded tightly, and did not come again to unbind the wound except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear, and for the fear of death which I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car for the evacuation of blood there was often, but he was healed entirely, and gave birth in place of the bone a hard child, and was of good temper and did not have any harm or opposite from all in all, nor air nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the backbone, then it is necessary to be done in this way: take a piece of rope, and pull it to the head of the bone which has been opened, and order that he not extend it upward; and put another piece of rope, larger than the first, on the head of the bone, and tie it to the hard child which is over the bone, and turn the head, so that you take out the hard child from below, and uncover the head where you see or feel the corruption, so that the corruption does not damage the child; and put a flame or a heated piece of metal over the bone to cover the corruption. And it is necessary to be done as often as one can see and feel the corruption, and also another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is rotten and will not open, and the rot is in the middle or in a part, then uncover the whole char; then put on it an ash twig, and then thread the corruption from one side to the other, and let the thread come out at the long end of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cover the rotten joint, and thread the bone where it is on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other pain but that of the cover; and if the corruption is at the hand's grip or at the foot's grip, then this is a very bad thing, nevertheless you should question this corruption, how it opens; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not do you harm; and know that the incisors and the threads for covering these bones are many, according to the appearance of the bones and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to adapt each instrument to each appearance of work, and know that the work will show you the instrument of which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so think about the instrument of which you will have need according to what suits you.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	In case of inflammation or injury; and when you have applied the medicine for corrosion by the cure of medicines, and it does not benefit, cover that member up to the point where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from death due to the malice, which is greater, of the defect of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, or seem to be burnt by fire, and the corrosion moves from member to member, taking hold throughout the body; if you hurry to cover it, and if it is due to the impact of certain venomous animals, such as scorpions of the sea and adders and similar things, cover it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, cover it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm; and if it comes up to the arm, cover it at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and do this whenever the corrosion comes or hurts: if it comes to the first joint, cover it after the other joint; and if it comes or hurts at the foot, cover all the foot; and if it rises in the leg, cover it at the knee joint; and if it comes up above the knee, there is no other remedy except to put the sick person to death; and the way of covering or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister the thread from one side, and another minister the thread from the other side, and loose the cloth which is between the threads at the wide spud, as much as the bone is uncovered; then cover or sew, and put a linen drape on each part, so that the thread does not touch the healthy part, and cause the patient more pain and infection by the stitch.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the pain comes while you are working, then cauterize the site thoroughly, or put some powder restraints on it; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and heal it until it is well; and I will tell you what happened at home in short: he got a blackness that looked like fire had burned it, and this corrosion came first in its due place from the foot, so much that it stained all the foot; and when the honor saw the corrosion, then it covered the foot with a layer of copper, and was healed; and a long time later the corrosion returned to its place on the palm of the hand, and came to me, and I put things that reflect after purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he said that I should cut off his hand, and I did not want to, that I had hope of impacting the matter; and I also doubted that if I would cut off his hand, that he would not die, because the virtues of man were weak; and he became completely desperate, and returned to his land, and covered his hand with a layer of copper, and was healed; and I only knew how to do this for another one, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No one should come to an abscess in the flesh, and delay for so long that it forms a large ball of pus; and then burst and escape, and remain inside as our servants do; and the skin that is above it is also thin like a flag, and does not run to the bone or nerves, and such a disease is called "healthy", and is not called "fistula"; but if it has become so long that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin should be cut from all around, and most especially when it is thin like a flag; and does not heal for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have promised that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick like a carpet, then treat it with Egyptian medicine made like this: take oil, and chalk, and equal amounts, and put the medicine in a vessel and heat it on the fire until the medicine turns red, and also becomes thicker than honey; and then take some of this according to your need, and make an emulsion with water and honey, and clisterize the breast, and extract the pus; and leave the medicine there for two hours, and then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is completely cured, and the pus is gone; and you should never clisterize with only water of ashes when this medicine is not present, but you should squeeze ashes from a vine stalk, and pour water on them, and then clisterize it, until you know that the breast is well cured; and if the patient cannot bear the pain, nor can the Egyptian medicine or water of ashes be used, then clisterize it with honey and wine which has been made sweet, that the honey has the property to cure and wash away, and the wine makes the disease better; and when you have done this, and know that the breast is completely cured, if the pus comes from the clistere that has been made, and is that you squeeze green ointment, and make it with oil of roses and wine; or you clisterize it with certain medicines and oils, of which I have spoken in the treatise on oils; and if the breach in the breast is small, and the tube for the clistere cannot enter, then widen it a little with iron, and put an envelop of the Egyptian oil, or basilicon oil, until it has widened enough; and if the wound is too wide, so that the clistere cannot enter, and if the breach from which the pus comes is above or below, then cut or raise it higher than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bowels are in perfect health, they should not be disturbed; and if you cannot cover the navel as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the bowels move downward as much as possible, for when the bowels are in perfect health, they should not be disturbed; and if you cannot cover the navel as you wish, prepare it in such a way: that the bowels move easily downward, leaving nothing of the bowel behind; and take medicines to strengthen it over the navel, and wrap them in linen cloths that cover all the navel; then apply the forceps to the navel on one side as widely as possible from the first, for the ligature is tied on another cloth according to the quantity of the navel hole, and placed on the navel hole to support the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and the one who is on the navel hole should often be removed to take off the bowel, and know what runs from the bowel, whether it is poison or pus or enough or digested or undigested; and take care that the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and how long the medicine has been extended in such a way, and you see the nature that rises on the navel hole, know that the breasts have already started to move, and approach them; and then remove it in the morning, or third day, and when you remove the wound, if you change another cloth, and renew the ligature.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if her breasts become sore and swollen after many days, know that her breasts do not ache.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons run long after a while, but you don't despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are some people whose breasts become sore and swollen after a long time, but their breasts do not ache; and if the breasts become late in healing, and are inflamed, know that this is due to a poison running into the breasts and causing inflammation; and if the breasts are swollen with pain after many days, know that the breasts do not ache; and if the healing of the breasts is delayed and is inflamed, then use the following medicine: take an initial batch of strong vinegar and add water to it and boil it; then use oil and rosewater and equal parts of vinery in a pan; then roast and blend it into powder; and add honey; and then use this mixture: make a paste from honey, mirre, and aloes, and add incense and rosin, and grind it, and then spread it on the breast; and never give it to drink as an aliment; but if you want to use herbs or compounds, grind them, and make powder of them, and put it on the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if this cure is long in healing, know that corruption has taken hold, and causes pain and inflammation in the bones, or in the limbs; so if one uses this cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the toe of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A bunion is a scar that grows out of the joint of the finger, or foot, or perhaps in another two places; and when it is irritated, and no attention is paid, then it comes to be a bunion that hurts and stings so much as to cause the root of the finger to become sore, and perhaps even the whole thing, and comes to have an ulceration reaching to the bone, so much as to cause a painful smell, and has two large joints, and is of a reddish color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not take, then you must take away all the surplus that has been stored up under the finger nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great aid if the bone is sound and the finger nail is healthy; and if the nail presses upon the flesh, and causes it to ache, then you must take away the root of the nail that presses, cutting it off sharply and lightly, and putting on top of the remnant of the nail burning and corrosive medicines in order to remove everything; then treat with salves as long as it remains healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	Et si la corrosion est dans l'os, alors le coupe et traîne-le, car tant que l'os est corrompu, il ne peut guérir ; et si tu vois que la corruption s'étend, alors soigne-le jusqu'à ce qu'il guérisse ; et s'il est blessé et douloureux, et sent une grande douleur, alors il faut le guérir en premier ; puis coupe l'ongle avec un couteau en coupant travers, et garde que la lame ne touche pas la chair qui est à côté de l'ongle, car le malade ressentirait trop de douleur ; et s'il arrive, alors met quelque chose pour apaiser.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	la douleur du cœur de la main
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Les deux membres qui naissent dans les mains de certains hommes sont parfois charnus, et parfois osseux, et n'ont jamais d'ongles, et aucune racine de la jointure ne nait en aucun d'eux.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se mute; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Cil who is born in the root of the joint if it is difficult to treat: if you hold him by the cup.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born in the heart of the joint, if it is right that you cut the rounded part up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable thread, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that come together by nature at birth, or by the assembly of a wound, or by fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you consider that you should cut the joint that is joined together by its natural forms; then place between two tents or drapes wet with oil rosin, so that it does not join together; or place between two pieces of fine cloth, until the joints are joined together as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Se soudemens comes to any of its two with the palm, so hold it firm as it should be.
des vils	of
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And the vile vis are large wrapped full of superfluous melancholy that come in many limbs of the body; and there comes in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you must not at any time administer a laxative to him, but cure him from the base.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure for iron is done according to two ways: one is that you cut it off, and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you leave the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size should be according to this way: raise the first leg of the warm water very well, until the large blood is thin, and then draw out the leg of the sick from above the knee down to the ankle; then cut the vein in one, two, or three places, then draw out and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one side chief to the other, as much as the virtue of the sick can bear; and then lie down, and order that he dye his meat by drinking black drink; and then begin the evacuation and the cure when the veins are empty, and rest on the sick.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The following is the translation of the text:
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if it is twisted and contorted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, it is necessary that you should tear it crookedly, but do not cover it; and handle it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And if it is twisted and contorted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, it is necessary that you should tear it crookedly, but do not cover it; and handle it as we have said before. The shape of the iron that one covers the vis with if it is curved, and does not cut, so that he covers the vein; and it is of large curve, because if it were thin, he would cover the vein, but being thick as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and perhaps it may grow elsewhere than in the legs, and such a thing happens that comes from the skin that comes from within the body winding itself and crawling, wound between skin and shield.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that there is a very great swelling in the leg, then the shape of it changes, and the wound begins to come out, just as the root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it cannot be reset, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at no time to this vein cut the hand, and least when it opens in the joint of the foot or where the foot is, and from there comes a great harm, and from which it often rains; then heal him as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers which are born between leather and horse
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buff disease," for it often affects buffaloes, and it is a small worm that borns between leather and cart, and goes up and down all over the body, causing pain at each member it touches, so that it comes off the skin where it has gone; and it is infected with pus, as if worms and scorpions and lice had entered into it; and one wonders about its malice, because when it goes through the body, and comes to the head, it goes to the oil, maybe by chance, and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you treat and draw it out, if you can only do so when he is: then first lie the joint on top of and tie it with a strong and very tight bandage, then lift up and draw out forcefully, and let it fall completely into the cart, and don't true it, but cauterize it with fire until he dies; and the greatest harm that he does, if he corrupts the oil as we have said; and if you see him coming with his head near the oil, then strain it out completely, then lift up and draw forcefully; and it is convenient to use the patient for purification of the corsages of soluble medicines for the bad humors putrid, and sear himself with meat that is rotten.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and moves from member to member; and I have seen this one that I told you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to treat a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and I saw a little swelling in the vein of her arm; and then after, I saw it rise up as if it were a worm in her shoulder, faster than anything else, like quicksilver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain left that place, and went into her shoulder, and then soon afterward corrupted all her body, until she came back to the other arm; then she told me that she was turning her body again around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how she moved from member to member, because I had never seen this disease move in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Anyway, I had heard many times that people with this disease sometimes feel pain in one place and then another, but I had never seen it. I thought that was because the woman's body was stiff and her veins were exposed; and because that swelling appeared suddenly, like a constriction; and I didn't see it fit for those who have stiff bodies and moist veins to be exposed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens like we have said, let it lie down and get better; and then bandage it tightly so that the wound does not move; and cauterize the wound; and if you do not see blood in your urine, let it be cured with pills made of rotten eggs, and serapin, and similar things.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	are various, according to their appearances and according to the places of their entry into the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	are of various shapes, for they have sharp or small or curvy or thick points; and some are two-edged, and some have tongues, and some pieces; and it poins in one member in a different way: or it poins in principal members, like the brain, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she dies, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: it is necessary that you wash yourself of this arrow extraction, for death comes after many preparations; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully extracted, take it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces the bone, and the medicine that is above the skull, is when there is a scald and a fever and a scorching in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of thought, and vomiting of food; and perhaps it does not come out through the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and if this sign appears to you, you must treat it, and draw out the arrow if it is stuck.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou quam, sont qu'elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s'elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the snot when it comes out is that without a plume of foam jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he gazes upward and shivers with cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the snot comes out in the covering of the foot, it is with great pain and great pain and sighing; and all the members move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the snot comes out in the stomach, perhaps some meat is vomited up.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow is lodged in the belly, and it does not come out through the intestine, then there is no hope for the cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow is lodged in the bladder, and it does not come out with urine, causing the patient to urinate frequently and feel great pain, know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if as with the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the ajutoire and the spine and the force and the cul and the legs, and the limb that seems to be affected, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it does not come out, then as I will tell you what happened to me, do the opposite.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to me that an arrow struck him in the jaw at the root of the nose: I tried to extract it, and I pushed it out from the other side with the help of a finger, and he was healed without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And throw in a quiver that the arrow falls into the oil grease of the paper dry, and the quiver was recovered, and there could be reached only the tip to the wood, and it was the quiver great of a Turkish arch, all I light without ears; The game was healthy, and no accidents came.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And throw a quiver from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabian quiver with ears; I knew the barbarians, and I waited until I threw it, and the Christians were healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And throw a quiver at home, which was knee or belly, and I thought he died; and then it passed XXX days, so his disposition did not change; I cut on the quiver, and engaged it, and threw it, and had no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow in his chest or back, and the wound is closed above; and hold the arrow within, and do not disturb its natural order, nor find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man who had an arrow in his face, and the wound was closed above; and held it so that he suffered great pain; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated a king's son who had an arrow in his lung, and it was a little傾向右邊，箭頭深埋在內；箭頭深陷在內，我被召來治療，三天后他去世了。
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with my finger and felt nothing; he felt no pain or tingling in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow; I put it on top of the plaster of the stomach because its legs don't swell; and I saw the legs of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for three days, and resolved the wound right away, and held him back a long time, so that he felt the arrow tip inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put the corrosive medicine on the wound for three days, trying it and feeling the tip of the arrow which was getting harder at its place; then I applied that medicine to the opening of the wound until the shape of the arrow became clear to me; and I waited three months, and then the wound opened so much that I had to use tweezers to pick it, pulling it from one side to the other, and I couldn't get it out; so I didn't stop from trying and inventing ways of instruments until I picked it with well-made tweezers, according to its shape which came out at the end of this chapter, till I put it back in place, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And I saw that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; but I restored it then, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Have you spoken about the quality of extraction of certain arrows, so that you place your cure on what I have not said, for the book cannot take all; but the master surgeons compare very little thing, and on what is present and failing, try nine operations, and nine instruments, in the dismemberment of strange things which come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows are not in the members unless they go through two ways: either by the place where they enter or by another part; and that which goes through one way is an arrow penetrating into its flesh, and never enters any more.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it no longer comes out, if you leave the flesh decay until it is rotten inside, and also if it is stuck in the bone, and it can't come out, if you wait a few days and then extract it; and then it comes out, and if it doesn't come out, if you pierce the flesh with a very fine thing all around, until the inner flesh is stretched, and then you pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes all the way to one of the lungs of the skull, and some of the accidents that I said may happen to the patient: do not remove it, but leave it as long as it remains even after a few days, for if the arrow comes out too soon, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not lodged in the bone but comes only up to the sinus, and the patient remains for a few days without any bad accidents, then the device for removing it can be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot come out, then I will give you advice on how to deal with it, as I told you; then treat the wound so that it heals well.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged so deep that it cannot be seen, then examine it with your hand at the full length; and if you feel it, examine it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot examine the wound because of its depth or the presence of the arrow, cut or bend the skin around it as much as you can, and then pull out the arrow; and be very careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out; and exam the wound thoroughly before removing the arrow.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull once, if the hair until the base is rotten, then try, for extraction it is difficult.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the pain of extraction makes you contrary, then introduce what we have said about the cure in his chapter; and guard against incising the nerve and opening a vein, and do not dare to extract the arrow without danger, soon or late, firmly or loudly; and place the patient according to the form he was when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or does not open anything of it, or the cure is swollen in place so that it can be seen or felt differently: then cut up until the pliers can take them, and then extract them: if it is now a jump.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it for a while longer, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out; and if there is an arrow in it, squeeze the arrow out completely; and if there is a nail in it, remove the nail by twisting; and if the arrow or nail can be removed, take care to administer a strong blow, so that the tip of the arrow or nail enters the handle of the instrument; then draw out again, and if the arrow or nail has been removed, squeeze the instrument from which the tip comes out, so that the arrow or nail will come out easily.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is lodged, then it is necessary that you cut all around the place where the arrow enters; if you can, do so, and then treat the wound as it is necessary to do.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow enters where the penis or in the belly or in the bladder or at the side, and it is near, then you can cover it, if you cover; and be careful not to cover the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if it is a job; and cure until it is well.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers that are used to treat arrows are similar to an eye, and thus the shape is this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And of many ways there are: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the butt-end is also like the beak of a bird, to fit to the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The pliers for fitting and for picking up are these.
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins from the chest
