If you have a large abscess that keeps coming back, most importantly when the opening of the vein is small, hurry and put a wet sponge on the spot with a little heat, and hold it for an hour; and it is right that you do this after the blood has left the vein, and if it stays in place after a few days, there is no harm done; and if you see it, put any of aloe or mirrour, juice of calument, mustard, or similar on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is abscess and appearance in the hand of the doctor; so put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be sure that you do not put your hand on anything of what we have said, because perhaps in a cut without the artery; but make him dry with poultice so as to harden the place, and then treat him with other treatment until he is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat every wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it flow until it is red, and if you see a lump, let it cool; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for those who are flat and foreign, and have a need to extract blood, let them make a larger wound and let the flames be wide; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and you must heal them little by little, and often, and the way of healing is saved from bleeding of blood and stretching of nerves, and it is better than long healing does not do.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose pulse is weak in health, it is fitting to give moistened bread in grape juice; if he is heated, then add warm water three or four times; and if he has a cold complex, then moisten it before health with moistened bread in musk syrup, or in honey syrup flavored with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and fennel, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he sweats in health, after the flow of blood, then it is fitting that he smell brew of wine and subtle aromatic syrup, and use the other things which we have said in the chapter or composition for fainting, to evacuate the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up his food and is healthy again, then it is fitting that he is healed little by little according to the quantity of his continuing virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who vomits after the first wound, and has a strong fever, if he heals seven hours after the first wound, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who vomits in another place, should he heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has fever inside his body, and it comes out through the pores, causing great fever; if so much is extracted, and the pore is enlarged as much as it can, then you should consider all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on his pulse when it heals, so that death does not come from the pores, and this happens many times when the healing is neglected; and you shall not consider when you separate the arm, and bring out blood the second time, and the pore is closed, that you press firmly; if it is bent, he should extend his arm gently, for that would be bad; but let it be until it heals the second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, as much as the blood that is frozen at the pore of the vein comes out, and put a piece of string soaked in water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, let it go and do not constrict it, as long as the abscess is drained.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if need be, to drain the blood a second time, if the vein is in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is attached to the vein at the base of the head because it is complex.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way of the vein is such that the patient holds his hand in warm water until the pulse is red; then let it move slightly so that the vein appears clearly, then make the cut across it, not wide nor long; and let the cut be next to the joint of the hand, and do not remove it, if it is in esteit, but rather let it remain there; for we put more trust in it when it is in esteit than when it is in a cold state; and the cut of this vein is more secure than any other vein, since it is neither an artery nor a nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The medicine for the right hand is all the ailments of the liver; and this is how it should be done: remove the hand and dip it in hot water until the vein has gone, if you can see it; and then cut off the end, and chop it up whole and whole, unless it grieves something; and don't chop it too much finely, because the nerves are all naked from the bone, and then put the hand back into the hot water, if it is stuck in the wound, and cannot be drawn out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and thread on it to hold it tightly together, and do the same for each finger.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The medicine for the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse; and do the same as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The medicine of the Sophene is good for all diseases that come about in the body, as are diseases of the feet, retention of wind, disease of the kidneys, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of this medicine is that the patient should dip his foot in hot water and rub it on the vein until it stops, and put it up on a joint at the foot; and if the pain is in the ankle, and then many rains go out from under it; cure it or the rain is larger, or at the ankle, so it hurts more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cure it on the foot, guard against the sores that are under it, and also cure it by walking as in riding; and let the flames go away.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot get them out, put the foot back into the water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the pain persists for the first time, then start again for the second above a little, because the leg is salt; do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and make it with the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leg of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle and its pain goes up to the knee when it is for pain.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its pain is that the patient goes in or out with it, and pulls it off the ankle 4 times by twisting, for otherwise does not open the vein; and if it opens, you must do it with all your strength, and pass more than once; and be careful to cut it, because the leg is up, and she is very relaxed.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then make a rain of the leg that opens or closes from the foot, and turn it slightly, and take care of the nerves; and make as much pain as you see, and then loosen the leg, and put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	the suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or of air, or of glass; and the suction is performed according to two ways: either by wounding and drawing blood, or not wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This is the first sentence of the text: "Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d'arain, ou de verre;
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Ventouses are made of horns, or of air, or of glass;" and if by necessity, or for habits, we administer them every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between; for there are some who, when they have to use ventouses, become heavy-headed; and those who experience redness on their faces, and in their chins, and darkness in their eyes; and those who taste blood in their mouths, and have a slippery tongue, and feel hunger and thirst; and those who dream, and see things that are not there.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even more so when it is hot in the month of July, we order them to be vented after three hours from daybreak.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And the bloodletting for headaches at the base of the skull ... it comes to a standstill, and it is not until all the blood has been evacuated from the whole body that this ventilation occurs; and this ventilation is in keeping with the bloodletting for the headache at the base of the skull, and it does not happen unless there is a cold complexion or someone has a fever, because this does great harm; and so it only happens if they fast in the evening, or if they have had a cold.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured often become dizzy, and so it is necessary to place the cup a little lower by doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And the bloodletting for the base of the skull and the temple is in keeping with the bloodletting at the base of the head and the temple, and so it is necessary to give a little less because it might cause dizziness or upset the stomach and intestines.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The windsations in the two ribs on the throat as the pains in the head, and obturations and headaches, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of the health of the bazaar; and it is necessary that you command the doctor that he express his hand to put it, that he does not cup the artery, and no corrently of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The windsations in the mouth are worth illness in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in place of the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windsations of the shoulders are worth illness that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windsations in the arms are worth as much as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and command the doctor that he does not sew too perfectly, for its bones are naked, and knows how to strip and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse that is on the back so it reaches the foundation of the heart, and the diseases of the soul, and it must be large and made of leather, so that it has the skill to milk well; and perhaps, if it were small, it would break; and it would make big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg ventouses open widely, for they draw blood from the whole body, and they are like the old pains of the feet and the legs, and of the bladder, and they remove the flowers; and they are in place of the two knees and the two ankles, but nevertheless they weaken the body over a long time, and bring death to many people with their dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the ventouse is that you put it first empty, and suck quickly, and then put it away, and stir evenly, and do not cease to do so until you see the red and inflamed place, and the pain of the blood; then let go, and remove the ventouses, and take care in the dispositions of the bodies, for there are some who have very sore hearts, and clear pores: it is good to hurt them once only, and to make large wounds, and a little bit deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the outside is thick, then he needs to hit twice: once to thin the blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the outside is very thick, then he needs to hit three times; and when we want to draw blood little by little, then we only need to squeeze once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to draw blood, then we should do so often; and if the outside is thick, then he should strike fully, and the end should be that the wound pierce suddenly, and cover with those who have thick and hard skin, and who are prone to bruises, you should moisten the places of the suction cups with oil that opens and dissolves: if it is in spring, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumis seed oil; and if it is in autumn, with nettle oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another type.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if it is too cold and oily, take oil of almonds, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if they have a sore that is dry and large, then it is not necessary to put oil on, but it is necessary to wash it after the cooling of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberries, or water of cucumbers, or water of porcelain, or other things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture, if it dries up like this, or with water of myrtle, and of sumach, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have too much moisture shall rise with old wine, or with water of oak, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other things; and it is not necessary to go to the bath before the cooling, but after the bath an hour or two; and you should not sleep after the cooling, but when it is necessary to cool down, then when it is hot.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware that those who are healing are coleric, and that their juice is too hot and inflamed; it is necessary that they drink cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in the shade, and similar things; and little apples, and char of chestnuts, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion should drink honey syrup and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and little soup, and little apples and small birds and pigeons; and on the day when it will be windy, they should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men triple or musk before the wind, or after, to strengthen the main members; and soften the juice, but it is only necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The windies that are put not to hurt are those that are put on the liver, and on the pancreas, and podagre, and on the belly and the buttocks and the kidneys and the hinch; for this member does not bear to be hurt on the olives, and it is only done so as to draw blood from one member to another, just as we put windies on the breasts when the disease is there; to remove the viscidity that is in the member, just as we put windies on the belly and the buttocks to weaken the member; and to relieve the pain, when there is an operation or a stone, it is relieved by its attractive virtue, perhaps the operation or the stone has left its place; and thus is done when they are put on the liver and the pancreas when there is a windiness retained, and these windies are emptied only to suck so little; and they are never emptied together, nor ever plain water, as in the disease of pleurisy, and in this way is the windie filled with hot water or with water in which herbs have been boiled that are appropriate for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus: It should be two hands wide and half a palm deep, and it should have a hole in the center about the size of an awl, just as for inserting an needle, and it should be made of leather, smooth on the outside, so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the member; and in the middle there should be a crossbar of leather or iron, to hold a grip, and there should be large and small ones according to the disease and the age of those who take them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of old people, and those of lean men are different from those of fat men.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And it should be placed on the member: take the grip of wax or linen, and put it in the middle of the suction cup across the bar, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the member, and these two should be on the hole that we have said, so that when you push, the vapor comes out, and take off the suction cup; and take the grip again as before, and renew it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of a lung disease, and all water, there is no knife or hole, but it is only when it is plain of water, and is placed on the limb so lightly; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	The text describes a treatment for a lung disease involving the use of suctions cups (ventouses) applied to the body. It emphasizes the importance of using cups that are small enough to fit in specific areas like the mouth and gums, and similar parts of the body. The text also advises against applying cups to the body when there is water present, as it could cause harm. Instead, it suggests waiting until the body is dry before applying the cups. When using the cups, they should be placed gently on the body without causing any discomfort or injury. The treatment involves placing the cups on the affected area and leaving them in place until they are clean and free of any buildup. Once cleaned, the cups can be reused.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, let the level rise in this way, and then of water very well, and then strain it; and if the levels are too late after the chest of the animals, so moisten a linen cloth with cold water, and put on, as long as the blood is stopped; and if there is more blood, so put on vitriole crushed, or gall, and similar things, as long as it is stopped; or you put on the level half of peeled peas, and let them sit until they get warm at the level, now it will stop; and if you need more, take other animals.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the animals do not want to take it, so rub the level with fresh blood, or you put in it a needle as long as the blood comes out of it, and then put them on, and soon as they feel the blood, they will warm up; and when you see that they are going to defecate, so sprinkle on a little aloe and sewed crushed, or ash, they will defecate now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapter of calumny is necessary many times in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of a fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the wise men have often poured on this chapter of calumny, that they never read any of the old books, or did not read a letter about it; and for this reason the science is strange to our land, for I never found one good book; and I know nothing, except by the science of the old books, which I have so studied that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by habit of my life; and I have described in this chapter of calumny what is contained therein, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is fitting that we say in this book the sums of speech and the chapters where wisdom sets forth her understanding, and holds fast to truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fractures, dislocations, twists, or strains occur in anyone, it is fitting that you quickly heal the sick person on both sides, unless there is some impediment; if the back is weak, or the hips, or the elderly; or if the tension is too tight, or too loose; and do not drink cold broths often, nor eat fatty foods, and do not fill yourself with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about the heat of the abscess, or the expansion of matter in the limb. If a disease returns to its original rule, then he should return to his previous treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meats that produce great thickness, or viscosity, like cooked flour in water, and rice, and eggs, and pies made from goat's milk, and cheese, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with great nutrition healing begins more quickly and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of old and weak people cannot properly heal or be joined together by nature's own process, nor those which are too tender, such as children's; but treat the broken bone with thick, strong flesh that hardens it and joins it together, until it is as strong as before; and do not at all omit to feed it on large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breakers are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is other than the break of the foot or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the shoulder, and another in twisting, as if the cutting of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that is all a small fracture.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own tool for restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place; and it is known that the break of the bone by what the turn is, and properly open by the sides, and a little pressure on the hand; and when there is no twistiness or bend in the foot, and the sick person does not feel much pain, there is no fracture; but it can have twistiness, or a cut, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move it by hand alone, but put on medicine that comes here after, and then restrained now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break that goes in arvol, and are the two parts separated, it is now necessary to put them at a point even, so that the apostemes come up and down; and if the apostemes come up, if he leaves for one day, as long as the apostemes are calm; then he puts it even with the mues that you can easily and cleanly, and know that the restoration of him is more easy than the restoration of the one where there are pieces; then restrain, as it is necessary here after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are pieces that break, if the estent of two parts, is hand or foot, or to your hand, it is a small member, or II strands, or a strand and to your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are set in place, then return by all means the additions in their places to the mues that you can, and keep that by your work no lesion comes to the patient nor pain; and fit well the two heads of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well in the hand if you think it is not good: if the drawstring is done well and does not pull too much, do not press as those who make them come by their work with hot and contracted member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, chastise the patient well that he does not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, neither turning, nor in any other way; and guard well that the member is so assured that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain, he is not in place, and it is necessary to put him in a position that he does not feel any pain; and guard well that he is placed correctly so that there is no tortuosity when he is restored; and the quality of the member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken member is diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arm and leg and hands: it is necessary to wrap linen cloth soft and fine; and those that are large, such as hip and thigh: it is necessary to wrap a broad and sturdy rope, for the broad ropes embrace all the large member, and hold it tight on all sides so that there is no gap; then tie light ligatures, III turns or IIII according to the size of the limb, and grasp the rope at the top end, then go up over the fracture and hold it less, so that the fracture is moved a little; and soften the rope a little and a little, until you press a lot of the healthy part, then take another rope, and return to the top of the fracture, and hold it gently, not too hard or too gently, as we have said in the first line about; then put between the ropes linen or cloth, so that they are all equal, then bind them well together, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, then put on something soothing to the abscess, and let it stand for some days; then strain it over your fingers, and let half a polecat's tail be boiling, or a piece of fust from which they make cleats, or palm fronds, and let it be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	And the strap that one puts on the break should be a little thicker and wider than the others; and it should be as far away from the member as it needs to be; then strain it over the fingers as you did with the first strap, and then tie it up tightly, just as in the first strap on the break; the tighter it is, the better; and the thread should be fine, not too thick or too thin, and of soft linen; for if the thread is thick, like the ropes that foolish people make their straps from, it is a great mistake, because the strap cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it only needs to be about two inches of space between each strap.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the hooks of the stars after extraction in their healthy state, then let them be bound with linen, or another kind of rag, so that they do not get cut.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the cure is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract stars from all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not appropriate to put stars on them before five or seven days, or more according to the urgency of the abscess that has broken out suddenly; and use here the ancient method of plasters for restoring breakages, dislocations, and twists: and this is that you take flour so that it adheres to the walls of a mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put on this composition, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster that restores the break to many different conditions, especially to women and small children, for it is not appropriate to make it too tight or too loose.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plastering: for breaking, dislocation and torsion: take the nettle, the fern, the onion, the asafetida, the arabic gum and mugwort, 10; mirr and aloe, 5; alchenille, 8; and reduce them to powder, mixing them with honey from bees. If the complexion of the body is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly restores broken bones, benefiting many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plastering for torsion: take mugwort and beeswax, 10; mirr and aloe, 9; acacia, 6; and black pepper, 10. Grind them well and mix them with honey or bee venom, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of plastering for joints and bones out of place, which soothes the pain immediately and repairs the size and fracture: take linseed, and soak it in water and cooked oil, and put it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cysts do not respond well, but they are good for soothing abscesses and properly relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make an ointment that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth-pine leaves, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make an ointment for healing bone breaks and reducing the swelling of an abscess: take fresh milk and mix it with wine, then apply it to the affected area.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of vetches, each of them in equal parts; grind them together and mix with wine, and the member is warmed, apply it with water or vinegar, and use this.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make an ointment that is more effective than the first one, which is used when the abscess is persistent and difficult to heal: take milk, wine, and water, each in equal parts, and apply it hot to the affected area.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and seed of flax, buckthorn, millot, and sanace, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each an equal part; and grind them up, and prepare a paste with salt water or sweet water or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, I hypocras says that one should not put anything on the broken member before it is healed, except a cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to me that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of poulticing that is good for lesion and pain: take wool and hair of sheep, or feathers of owl, and wormwood, and silk evenly, and grind them up, and make a poultice and put it on him.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then let it rest for a little while, and take care that the patient feels no pain or that his nose does not move out of place; if pain comes to its place, or itching, or lack of rest or swelling, then hurry and let it rest, and apply the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sea sponge moistened, and dip it in water, and lift up the leg, as long as the itching ceases and the pain is calmed; then leave it to rest for an hour, then put on another dry cloth, wet with water or oil and tie it to a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is warm; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and the pain goes away, then start again gently, and a little plaster, and do not pull it as hard as before; and gently until it is well.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is chafed and red and painful and swollen all around it, and you have to use poultices and ligatures, then start again, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb does not come to rest at all of what we have said, if it does not stay in place except for three days or four or five or seven; and never leaves it for more than twenty days, according to what you see, until the break comes closer to the shoulder, then restrain it more than before, and make the flesh grow thicker, as I have said before; and if you see that the leg is drying up more than is necessary, then dunk it in hot water every time you take it off, and let it air dry for a day or three, by this work therefore cut off the bad blood from the limb, and carefully remove what is causing the deformity, which straightens out the limb: that is painful, and if it is full of fear, and I see no other thing than to leave it and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways to break up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are various ways to break things up, and there are different shapes and causes. For there is a breaking that is done by the impact of an arrowhead, and the collarbone breaks all the way down to the shaft which goes through it, as if it were made with a hatchet; and for this reason this type of breaking is called "hatchet-work".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or an arrowhead breaks the bone from above without piercing it, and for this reason this type of breaking is called "absolute"; and there is a wound from these two great or small breakages.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	Or if there is percussion inside, or an edge, or a collarbone of stone, or falling on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a breaking that approaches the tendon which is over the bone, or is under it, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that has penetrated the bone as fine as a hair, and is a small fracture, for this reason it is called "capillaire"; and if the wound is made by hitting a stone, or by falling, or by some other thing, and thus a piece of the bone enters the body, and the head of the bone is so shaped as the smith shapes the iron when he hammers it on the anvil; if it goes inside the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens often to those who have their heads wet with water, as the head of a child; and these kinds of fractures are made in many ways, as I will speak about them in due course.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by traction on them, and by the inspection of wounds, and by the cart that is before it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is caused by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubbed it in, thus opening the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for the fracture, take care as to the accidents of the disease, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of understanding, extension, paleness, feverishness, or hair growing furiously red and other similar signs in many conditions, so it cannot be healed by doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any hopeful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the birth comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most that you can do.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone may not decay, and the accident that we have spoken of may come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, so it is that you split the broken part in such a way: and it is that you press the head of the patient, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more softly than you can, and if the removal of blood comes to discover the bone, or abscesses, help yourself with what is convenient, and it is that you fill the place of drapings wet with oil rosin; and let the wound rest as long as the abscesses are calmed, and be sure of the removal of blood; then begin to break the bone, and this is done according to II ways of work: one way is that you split a very narrow part in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I bottle another way more than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various lengths of scales, some short and others long, and they are pointed, and made of iron; and do it lightly, so as not to hurt the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is tough and hard, it is necessary that you pierce behind it, so that you put scales with bars on top of it, not completely piercing through the bone but leaving a margin or circle above it so as not to let the tip go beyond the bone; and you need to have many, so that each comes in its place at the end of the bone, so that you have bars for all of them; and this is the form of the three ways of making bars:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing behind the bone is that you place the bar on top of the bone, and turn it back two or three times until you know that the bone has been pierced; then put the bar elsewhere a little further on, and do the same all around, then chop the space between the pits, and do it more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you hold the bone in your hand, or with any of the tools that you have, such as pliers, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinews.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have broken the bone and treated it, if you notice that you are keeping the marrow which is being extracted from the bone with all other instruments that resemble an incision, but it should be softer and finer than the other incision; and if it does not hold any small bones or scales, but cuts the bone lightly on the tools; then cure the wound with tender and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of cauterization is that which Galien says, which is stronger; and the fire is very hot, and this is what he says.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you discover a part of the bone, where the break is open; so that when you have discovered that part, you put the head of this lens-shaped incision there, from which it gets its shape.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Et ne trenche mie d'une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers loz; puis fier d'un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l'os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s'elle est aerse a l'os, si l'oste legierement, car on l'oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is wet in two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit with a small mallet on top, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and take good care of the tendon that is attached to it; if it is caught on the bone, then carefully cut the bone, for one cuts the bone well without hurting, and without fear.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are dealing with very sharp razors, and then with even sharper ones, and do not stop doing this as long as it is necessary.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle shaves, you must bring about the cause according to his setting; and this is a thing that is not properly replied to for one who has set his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the leech is uncovered, you should take a linen drape, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it with oil, and put it on the wound; then take another doubled drape, II or III, and moisten it with wine and oil, and put it on the first drape; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not grieve the leech, then remove it after a day or two, until the abscesses are healed, then wash them off, and apply medicines as roots, and flour of times, and powder of incense, and alchimist, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer medicines that have no taste of mordation; and be careful that the wound is clean, so that you do not allow it to get dirty, nor allow a bow to assemble upon the silk cloth of the brain, for if it correrts and pierces, it brings great misfortune upon the patient; for when you put something sharp on the leech, if it stings from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.

Take great care therefore that no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful whether it is or not. Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that the two bones above are never broken by a fall, for they are cartilage, and they do not break unless they bend or twist, and then heal.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you should drill a small hole in the nose or buttock above the bone, and make an even hole in it by your little finger, and to the opposite side, until the bone regains its natural form; and do this with care so that the patient does not feel pain because of your work.

Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind the other with something else, if the break is there; and let the strips be so thick that they fill the holes of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no one should restore it without wetting the strips first; each day they must be changed.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that this is not good, but it is necessary that the strips be wet with olive oil and powder of malachite; then leave the strips, until the bone has hardened and the joints have healed.

de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not very deep, and it is not shattered into two pieces, but rather twisted inside, then one should handle it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is fitting, if the break is on the right side, that you insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left side, then insert your index finger from the right hand into the break slightly, and make it equal with the left hand, and fix it.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is on the second side, then it is fitting that you equalize the two sides with an extension, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement occurs from within at the site of the break, then you should strap it with a gold, silver, or silk cord; then put a double cloth on top of the broken jaw, and put a large, well-made piece of leather on top of it that is as long and wide as the jaw, and tie it securely in place with knots; and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure has changed, if you let it rest for three days, and then put back what has been changed; and put plaster on, of powder from the mill with a lot of egg or flour from millet, after you have taken off the cerotte; and put on another lighter plaster, and if the plasters hurt, and the disposition of the sick does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times are healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses arise, if you administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not take a piece of the bone out; if subtle of the osteotomy are the instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, if you open it by fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.
