Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if he is dislocated in front, so he returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and proud of the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not return to his place, so administer a strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and they tint them two ministers, so that he does not move at the extension; then turn the arm of each part, then that you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when you see the joint with the joint to his hand, so oil it with no oil to soften the joint, then tighten the joint firmly, until it recovers; and when it is in its place, put it on plaster dry with ashes of alf, and strain it firmly, and tie the arm to the neck of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then undo it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then untie it and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well fitted, then restart the plaster and the bandage, and leave it like this for some days, until it is firmly set.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint has been put back in place, and it moves around, then bathe it and rub it well, and press until it is relaxed; or you put a layer of sheep's fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let him go in or swim; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the fat back on, and then go in or swim; and do this II times or III, until it is well; and if you see, then put a wet sheep's skin on it, heated with butter, and strain it over; then bring it back to its place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is less stable than that of other joints. However, it is necessary to return it to its place immediately, while it is still dislocated, so that the joint swells or an abscess develops.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when you bring it back, place the injured hand on a table and stretch it out. Keep your eyes focused on its position so that you can see if it is in place, and then put it back into place; place the patient's palm down on the table with their fingers spread out.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's palm down on the table and spread out their fingers.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good; but if the extraction of the pus from the abscesses does not relieve him, then leave it like this for now.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, then the joint is twisted; and do not bother the patient unless his hands are wet, and he can't extract anything at all: then know that the nerves or arteries have been cut, otherwise there is only one way to extract it by means of a delicate cauterization, and perhaps there is nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put it on the pus as we have said, then extract it and leave it for 5 days, then take it off and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he can't move it well, and there is no fracture, if the hot water makes it moist, and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand are not displaced at each end, nor on the back of the palm or belly; then they are bent, and shift the dislocation to the pouche until it returns, then support the head of the finger with your thumb, and turn it towards the part where it is joined; and let it rest for a day, and then put it in line that day; and from then on, if he has moved, turn him again, and let him move, and reline him; and do this often, until he is tight, and do so too, if it is displaced at the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until he is well; and do also, if it is displaced from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand are not displaced at each end, nor on the back of the palm or belly; then they are bent, and shift the dislocation to the pouche until it returns
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the neck or collarbone is dislocated, or multiple dislocations occur, there will be no cure unless it is quickly treated, for death comes swiftly to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the exudations are without taste or scent, that it cannot be held, and often one of the limbs becomes soft, or the two arms or one, and often the esplanade moves in four directions; this is called "gilbosier": if this comes from childhood then there is no cure or recovery for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting down or percussion or similar things, the ancient ways of curing with great words did not bring much good at all; but I have simplified them according to my intention, and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the Gilbosier which comes from behind, there is no beginning or cure; and likewise that which comes straight in two directions, and cannot be cured except by that which properly comes from behind, as I say; it is that the patient should lie flat on his back in an equal position, and have the straining taken off him so that he does not hurt himself; then set a piece of wood at the head forming a platform, and another between the feet, and tie a rope to the head and the other end to the feet; and let the two ministers fasten the ropes, one to the head and the other between the feet, among the two logs; and let them be well fastened, as we have said, and the mirer sets his palms on the esplanade forming, until he revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	Et s'elle ne revient par ceste cure, si prenne une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l'espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l'autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu'il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And if this cure does not succeed, then take a table three arms long, and shave off a section of the wall, and place the patient on one side, and pour water from the table onto the wall, then set the middle of the table over the spine; and place the doctor's tools over the other head of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see anything, do it with a turner that turns in your hand.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, put on plasters with lots of wax, and then the staples, and then the stake of a tablet of three fingers long, which purifies his place of the gimbosity and the part of the spine healthy, then tie him with a thread as we have said, and use the subtle healing methods until he is well; and if anything comes at the end of health, administer softening and soothing medicines with the stake that we have said before; and never give him a piece of lead, and never does the appearance come in the back spine from the back, and take care that it is dislocations; and this is the bone that opens up, so do not have any presumption: by chance would bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches that the joints of the hip and shoulder come only in dislocations, not at all like the other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, before and behind; and more inside, and less before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocations inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy, it is farther away, and more bent than the healthy, and cannot double the sick knee; and this is the place which is swollen and hot with an abscess, for that the head of the thigh comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which comes outside is that this accident is opposite to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that which comes before are that his leg is right according to the completion; nevertheless, it does not double the knee with pain, and when one makes it walk, it cannot go forward, and holds back its urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he passes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has been behind, if he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and is this leg more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hipbone is in its place among the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And the signs of him who has been behind, if he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and is this leg more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hipbone is in its place among the ribs. If this dislocation is old, and it takes a long time to heal according to its condition, then there is no cure; and it only comes that he has presumptiveness.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those who have a fresh dislocation, and there are the four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to reset the joint, and make it tighten and go away, and turn it from side to side; perhaps it will come back, and there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, then you should prepare the patient very well, and hold his leg very firmly with two hands, or with one ligament that is tied to the knee; and another minister extends his hand over him in such a way that he can bottle his hands from his knees, then ties him by a ligature on the thigh; and another pulls his hair out at the roots; and they stretch upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains so.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	And this way of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you should place the patient on their back, and then tie the ligament to the root of the thigh, and let go of the skin, then extend the ligament upwards towards the pubic bone, and upwards towards the forceps; then another minister will embrace the large tendon of the thigh, and will stretch it away from the body: then if it returns to its place now; and this way of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this way that we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the sick person together with a strong rope under the heels, and on the thighs, and the sick leg should be extended more than the other; then hang it on the head of a pole, and above the ground are II long arms; then order the minister that he embraces the head of the hip, and let others embrace the hip firmly, for the joints will now return to their places.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are away, then lie the sick person down, as we have said in that which has gimberly, and stretch the rope properly on the sick leg, and on the thigh also; then put II torches, I at the head and another under the feet, then insert one torch between the hips of the sick person according to his form; and let there be wet drapings around, so that it does not burn the sick person, then spread each minister towards him, and the master should put his hand on the dislocation equally.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, set on .ie. a table, and press it thus as we said in the gibosity, and lay the patient on the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are forward, if it is necessary to extend the leg of the patient inwards, and according to what I have said; and put his weight upon the sound side, then press with the other hand, and bring it forward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocations are backward, if it is not necessary to extend the leg of the patient outward, nor to raise him up on the ground, but rather that he should be placed as if the leg were forward, as we said in regard to the laying down on the two knees; and let him lie on his face, and stretch the bandage thus as we said before, and press it on the joint against the table; and it will be complete when the patient extends his legs, and they are even; then tie the bandages, and apply the plaster, and tighten it with a strap, so that the knee does not move; and let him rest three or four days, then untie him, and make him jump about, as long as the members remain firm.
de la dislocation dou genoil	from the dislocation of the hip joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The hip is dislocated in three ways: namely, inwards, outwards, and backwards; do not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient that he should bend his leg to his knee, and if it does not bend to his knee, knowing that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place his back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his kneecap with your palms, and pull it between your two hands, then bend the two sides of the knee cap; and have others extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that he bends his leg to his knee comfortably; and put the paste on, and make him walk with his leg bent to his knee, and hold it together for three or four days, then remove it; and do not work the patient to walk, until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the members are not at their place, if one administer a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation from the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never dislocated, nor completely displaced inward or outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are such that the ankle is displaced, and the tend to the part where it is displaced: one should gently ram it back into place when it is only slightly displaced, and one must gently extend it with his hands.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is displaced from the top, you should make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg away from under the body; then you bring the foot up to your right hand, and then to your left twice, and then you keep it in the air, and blow strongly on the foot; and do this twice, as we have said, by blowing and bringing the foot up: if it comes back, it is good; but if not, you begin the work again, for it will come back; and if he cannot come back like this, you make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put a staff firmly in the ground between his hips, and tie the sheets around him so that he does not bleed; then you extend the healthy leg away from under the body with your hands or legs; then each minister extends evenly, and the staff is kept in place between the hips of the patient to hold the patient down while it is being extended; then the doctor who performs the dislocation holds it in his hands, and other ministers extend the injured leg away from under the body with their hands or legs; then you blow strongly on the foot, and do this twice: if it comes back, it is good; but if not, you begin the work again, for it will come back; and if he cannot come back like this, you make the patient lie on his side, and extend the injured leg away from under the body with your hands or legs; then you blow strongly on the foot, and do this twice: if it comes back, it is good; but if not, you begin the work again, for it will come back.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it has set, then put on the plaster and press it down, and form the splint, and fasten the leg to the foot, and guard the tendons behind the ankle so that the bonds are not too tight; then leave it for II days or III, and let the bonds become loose if the splint; then remove it by the third day or the fourth, and no longer let the patient walk for IV days; and if he walks before this term, it is not yet certain that he will still dislocate.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses come to a head, so that you calm it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is well.
des dois	the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, so that they are nicely extended without work, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocations are in no way out of the two feet of the leg, then you make the patient sit on a plain or flat table completely upright, and put your foot on what opens up from these joints, then press it down forming, until he has recovered; and when it is even, and there is nothing more open, then set up the splint with II beams, then form the splint, and leave it for III days, then remove it; and let him rest, until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not learned in the art and have not long practiced it, and if you are not compassionate and tardy, do not be bold; and use at the beginning soothing remedies for the abscesses, and leave the patient in the hands of God, unless you see a chance for health; and when you see a chance, now restore the limb to its place, so that the abscesses come; and when the limbs are in their places, administer soothing remedies, and cure the wound as it should be, with ointments that dry it up; and if there is a fracture, and small bones are dislocated, then repair them, and do what we have said for simple illnesses; and guard yourself from entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will lead you astray according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming and strengthening your body.
Amen	Amen
